上海郵政管理局封發郵件時刻表

上海各支局皆可寄交掛號快遞航空郵件及辦理滙兌儲金等事務

1936.07.15

The Second Plenary Session Concluded Yesterday; The Third Meeting Resolved to Send a Telegram of Condolences to Wang; Passed the Draft of the General Assembly Declaration

(Nanjing) The Second Plenary Session held its third general meeting at 9 a.m. on the 14th. The attendees included Central Executive Committee members Chiang Kai-shek, Feng Yuxiang, Yu Youren, Sun Ke, Wu Tiecheng, Ye Zhengcang, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, Ju Zheng, Chen Lifu, Wang Quansheng, Luo Sang Jian Zan, Wang Boqun, Ye Xiufeng, and 88 others; observers from the Supervisory Committee Lin Sen, Zhang Ji, Cai Yuanpei, Yang Hu, Shao Lizi, Chu Minyi, Xu Yongchang, Pang Bingxun, and 24 others; observers from alternate Executive Committee members Gu Zhengding, Lai Lian, Jing Hengyi, Xiao Zheng, Li Renren, Yang Yongtai, Cheng Tiangu, Zhang Zhen, Huang Shi, and 37 others; observers from alternate Supervisory Committee members Lu Dangping, Lei Zhen, Pan Yunchao, Cui Guangxiu, Sun Ruiya, and 18 others, totaling 162 people. Kong Xiangxi chaired the meeting.

Reported Matters (1) Reading of the minutes of the second meeting; (2) Secretary's Office report on documents.

Matters for Discussion (1) The Party Affairs Group of the Proposal Review Committee reported on the submitted work reports of the Standing Committee and the three departments of Organization, Propaganda, and Public Training. After the meeting's review, the results are reported as follows: Upon reviewing the work of the Standing Committee and various departments for the six months since the closing of the First Plenary Session, it is generally found that they have been able to diligently implement the principles determined by the Fifth National Congress and the guidelines resolved by the First Plenary Session. However, in practice, it seems that the established policies have not been effectively applied to increase the vitality of party affairs and further solidify its foundation. This is because the environment is inevitably subject to obstacles, and party affairs and the actual political and social situation have not been able to advance simultaneously in a suitable manner, which is the crux of the problem. Therefore, it seems necessary to make significant improvements in the future. Whether this is appropriate is respectfully submitted for public decision. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinion. (2) Proposed by the Presidium: 1. A case to send a telegram of condolences to Chairman Wang Zhaoming in the name of the Second Plenary Session. Resolution: Passed. 2. Draft declaration case for the second plenary session. Resolution: Amended and passed. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

Circumstances of the Closing Ceremony of the Plenary Session

(Nanjing) After the adjournment of the third general meeting of the Second Plenary Session at 11 a.m. on the 14th, the closing ceremony was held in the Central Auditorium after a short break. The participants included more than 160 Central Committee members, the same as those at the third general meeting, and more than 100 staff members from the Secretariat of the Plenary Session, totaling 300 people. At 11:10 a.m., the ceremony was declared open. Chairman Feng Yuxiang first led the orchestra, and then led everyone in performing the rituals. Feng then delivered a closing speech. After the speech, Feng read out the General Assembly Declaration. After the reading, the ceremony concluded. The Second Plenary Session opened on the morning of the 10th and lasted five days until the 14th, with one preparatory meeting, three general meetings, one review meeting, and four meetings of the Presidium. Important cases such as the organization of the National Defense Conference were passed, and the intentions of the General Assembly were also fully stated in the declaration. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

(Nanjing) Feng Yuxiang said in his speech at the closing ceremony of the Second Plenary Session: Although the term of this Second Plenary Session was not long, the spirit was very good. In such hot weather, everyone gathered together calmly to discuss all major plans for national salvation. Such a good scene cannot be seen elsewhere. It is really a very good phenomenon. The most important and noteworthy thing in this conference is the National Defense Conference. This conference can be said to be a national salvation conference. It is really very important. The closing declaration of the plenary session mentioned that we hope that our determined comrades will participate in this conference, contribute their opinions to the central government, and work together unanimously. What is especially important is that some comrades who are not very clear about the intentions of the central government should do our best to make them all clear. We must truly and frankly speak for the nation and the people, so that they can understand the intentions of the central government and resolutely stand on the same front with the central government. Only in this way can our nation have a way out. In the meetings of the past two days, two gentlemen reported on the issue of national defense. This is because we were afraid that some of our comrades were not clear about it, so we specially gave a detailed report to make everyone understand the central government's preparations. Today our meeting is over. After the adjournment, we hope that all comrades will, in the spirit of the meeting, work hard and strive forward in accordance with the teachings of the Premier, to save our country and revive our nation. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

Full Text of the Declaration of the Second Plenary Session

(Nanjing) The declaration of the Second Plenary Session is as follows: More than half a year has passed since the Fifth National Congress and the First Plenary Session. Looking back on this period, the internal and external environment has become increasingly difficult and dangerous. The sincere spirit of the people of the whole country, amidst extreme anxiety and suffering, to face the national crisis together has become increasingly profound. What the people earnestly expect from our party is how to unite the people's will and strength to save the country, resist the current foreign insults, and preserve the survival of the nation. What our party has been persistently and responsibly doing, exerting its greatest efforts, is also aimed at this goal. At this plenary session, the attendance of comrades from the central government was unprecedented. Most comrades, either shouldering heavy responsibilities or having not been to the capital for a long time, all came to the capital to discuss major plans together. The abolition of the two southwestern organizations was proposed by the majority of comrades from Guangdong and Guangxi, which is sufficient to eliminate the divisions and estrangement since the Fourth National Congress, demonstrate the actual centralization and unification of the party and the country, and eradicate the conspiracies of slander and division. It can be seen that sincere unity has long been a common sentiment, and the determination to overcome difficulties together is increasingly evident. After examining the external environment and reviewing the internal conditions of the country, the plenary session seeks to clarify to all party comrades and the people of the whole country how to truly unify the will to save the country and achieve the goal of national salvation. The Fifth National Congress, with its focus on national salvation, has already clearly indicated to us the correct and unchanging direction and basic essentials. It believes that in China today, without striving through self-imposed hardship and thoroughly renewing awareness to establish a "modern state" with developed and abundant human and material resources, there is no way to overcome the dangers of the environment and lay the foundation of the country on a solid foundation. For the main points of resisting foreign insults, it also clearly indicates the limits of choosing national policies, supplemented by the determination of the final sacrifice. All resolutions are not only believed by party comrades as the truth of national salvation, but also recognized by the general patriotic and enlightened citizens as a point of common effort. The plenary session reviewed the central party and government measures over the past six months, believing that they have indeed been able to adhere to the direction entrusted by the Fifth National Congress, striving hard and achieving considerable progress in an environment of internal troubles and external aggressions. In terms of diplomacy, although the degree of national crisis is deepening and becoming more serious, the central government has responded sternly and dealt honestly, striving to bring diplomacy back to the right track. The efforts of the soldiers of Hebei, Chahar, and the entire country to maintain national rights have significantly changed the international view of us, and the hope of peaceful negotiations has not been completely extinguished. In terms of internal affairs, reforms such as currency reform, financial stability, construction progress, as well as suppressing bandits and preventing natural disasters, have all achieved rapid and significant results after enduring hardships. The timely promulgation of the draft constitution and the scheduled convening of the National Assembly are proceeding in an orderly manner, not only showing good faith to the people, but also gathering the minds and talents of the whole country to jointly plan for national salvation. As for completing the organization of a "modern state," the main focus is not only on striving to build the national economy and strengthen self-defense capabilities in the material aspect, but also on restoring the inherent morality of the nation and awakening national consciousness. Efforts should be made to cultivate public training and student training in various places, which are sufficient to unify the will to save the country and arouse the spirit of defending the country. At the same time, universal development of national education is sought, and opportunities are sought for unemployed youth to serve. The main purpose is to enhance the morality and strength of the people, implicitly strengthening the foundation for national defense, and continuously strive to complete the organization of a "modern state." If we can work together consistently and move forward along this path, we will surely establish the foundation for national rejuvenation. This is what all wise men in the country are working with and deeply believe in. Moreover, the spirit of the so-called "modern state" lies in the unity of strength and the strictness of discipline. There has never been a case where scattered strength can resist insults, nor has there ever been a case where lax discipline can build a country. Today, if the whole country, from top to bottom, sincerely wants to resist foreign insults, it must cherish the unified situation achieved through ten years of hard work and sacrifice, and absolutely abide by the public discipline related to the national life. If we can train discipline in education and organization, the people can be united and not scattered, and the country can naturally increase its strength. If we can respect discipline in politics and military affairs, the central government and the local governments can be like the arm being used by the body and the finger being used by the arm, and the remnants of separatism and feudalism can be swept away. The country's strength will have accumulated increase and true unity, and the solid foundation needed for the country's struggle against foreign countries will be established. In short, the way to survive and save the country is none other than resisting insults, and the prerequisite for resisting insults is to concentrate all the strength to save the country under the central command, unify its pace, and consolidate its front. Therefore, unity and discipline are the unshakable iron rules for resisting insults and saving the country, and the unification of military and political orders is the minimum requirement for completing the organization of a "modern state." This is what those who talk about national defense must know, and what all compatriots today must understand. The recent changes in Guangdong and Guangxi, revealing the banner of foreign aggression and shaking the foundation of unity, have added fear of disintegration to the country amidst its worries and difficulties. On the one hand, it is sufficient to reflect the difficult and complex environment in which China is today. At the same time, it also proves that if the various parts of the country cannot maintain strict discipline and unity, it is not enough to establish a foundation for external resistance, but will only aggravate the national crisis. Since the occurrence of this incident, the central government has felt the danger of national affairs and cherished the strength of the country. It has always been trying to handle it carefully with peaceful methods, hoping to reverse the dangerous situation invisibly and promote the awareness of unity. Fortunately, public opinion across the country has been able to distinguish right from wrong, speak up and advise, and the people of Guangdong, the source of the revolution, have long been influenced by revolutionary doctrines and will not be shaken by deceptive words. The officers and soldiers of the Guangdong army, navy, and air force have been able to reveal justice, cherish the glorious history of the revolution, and do their best to maintain the unity of the country. This is what all patriotic compatriots in the country are happy about, and it is also the true will and strength of our country during the period of serious national crisis. However, the Guangdong military authorities have already initiated dissent, acted freely, violated the discipline of the party and the state, and shaken the foundation of the revolution. Although the central government has been patiently tolerant, there is still no sign of repentance. According to the national discipline, it should not be tolerated by the people. The plenary session is deeply saddened by the changes in Guangdong and Guangxi, and in view of the difficulties of national affairs, it is unwilling to lightly use the limited strength to impose internal sanctions. Therefore, it still adheres to the Premier's spirit of generosity and strives to eliminate the changes politically and bring them back to the right track, only seeking to ensure that the country's political and military orders can be effectively implemented from now on, the distinction between right and wrong is clear, and the laws and regulations are not damaged. Not only does it not want to make harsh demands on this incident, but it also traces the causes of estrangement and errors, and seeks to eliminate the basis for alienation and exploitation. For military comrades who have a history of joint revolution, they are still willing to entrust them with the authority of national defense and seek further unity. At the same time, it is also felt that responsible comrades in various places all have the spirit of saving the country, but there are few opportunities for joint discussion. At this critical moment of survival, it is even more necessary to concentrate efforts and share the heavy responsibilities. Therefore, the National Defense Conference was established, hoping to gather the thoughts and talents of the whole country, express good plans for saving the country, and plan for the safety and enrichment of the entire national defense, in order to establish the foundation for survival and national salvation. The plenary session firmly believes that this measure will be in line with the national desire to save the country and will create a force of cooperation and unity. It is also necessary to inform our compatriots across the country that the more difficult and dangerous the situation of the country, the more orderly and solemn the will and actions of the people should be. The people who take it upon themselves to save the country and the responsible central government must have thorough trust and strong perseverance. Those who can do this will prosper, and those who do the opposite will perish. This has always been the case, both in ancient and modern times, both in China and abroad. It must have the determination to sacrifice and fight in order to undertake a long-term and arduous undertaking. China has suffered from many internal diseases and is bound by external forces in the past 100 years, and is also in the vortex of international conflicts. It can be known how difficult it is to build a country. Our party, upholding the Premier's legacy and shouldering the great task of revolution, can expect the arrival of dangers and difficulties. It will never slacken its responsibilities due to the difficulties of national affairs. It is also well aware of the century-long interests of the nation and will never allow it to be taken lightly. The sacrifice of one person or one party is a small matter, while the sacrifice of the country and the nation is a big matter. Our country has already reached this extraordinary period unprecedented in history. The correctness of the decision at this time is related to the continuation of thousands of years of history and the peace and security of the nation for thousands of generations. Therefore, not only should our party, which is responsible for building the country, be patient and calm in dealing with events, but also all our compatriots should bear all the responsibilities for the past history and the future of the nation at this critical moment of survival, recognize the responsibilities of the times, and face them with an absolutely serious and cautious attitude. In short, the current situation in China is that if we do not seek survival with a determined heart, we will not be able to obtain security. If we do not act with unity across the country and take orderly steps to seek salvation, we will not escape the crisis of being defeated one by one. Therefore, at this time, the people of the whole country can only, based on the sincere intention of saving the country, give the central government thorough trust, be able to unite and maintain unity, and consolidate the central government, so that it can bear its responsibilities and use the coordinated strength of the whole country to save the country and protect the nation. Then, no matter how difficult the environment is, we will definitely be able to reverse the crisis and create a great cause of rejuvenation. Otherwise, if the will is not unified, the steps are not uniform, we will build a house on the road, undermine discipline, and the foundation will be damaged. Even without foreign enemies, we will inevitably collapse and cannot be saved. Our party has been entrusted with the heavy responsibility by our compatriots across the country. It must do its best to use its mind and talents, and carry it through to the end, even if the situation becomes more dangerous, it will never give up in the midst of encirclement and attack, and will establish the foundation for the sound organization of the country for my China, and seek permanent survival for my nation. What we dare to solemnly declare to the people is that the country is in this extraordinary situation, and we can only seek the unity of the people across the country with the greatest tolerance and care internally, and we will never tolerate any fact of infringing on territorial sovereignty externally, nor will we sign any agreement that infringes on territorial sovereignty. If there is a fact of infringement on territorial sovereignty, and if all political methods are exhausted and ineffective, and the fundamental survival of the country and the nation is threatened, then we must make the determination of the final sacrifice, without any hesitation. This is the policy determined by the Fifth National Congress, and now it is further interpreted and revealed, in order to be shared by comrades of the party and compatriots across the country. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

The General Assembly Sends a Telegram of Condolences to Chairman Wang

(Nanjing) Before the opening of the Second Plenary Session, the Chairman had telegraphed from Germany to the General Assembly, requesting leave. Now, the General Assembly replied on the 14th with a resolution of the Third Meeting, sending a telegram of condolences to Wang in the name of the General Assembly. The telegram was also issued by the Secretariat of the General Assembly. The text of Wang's telegram and the General Assembly's telegram to Wang are recorded below: (1) Wang's telegram: Received your telegram while ill, sorry that I could not rush back. I believe that the Fifth National Congress has determined the direction of foreign and domestic policy. At this time, we should earnestly follow it and solve the problems based on it. Sincerely, Dong. (2) The General Assembly's telegram to Wang: Respected Chairman Wang Jingwei, I admire your advice upon reading your telegram. Comrades are deeply grateful that you are mindful of national affairs while recuperating. I respectfully send my regards, and wish you a speedy recovery to good health to return to the country and preside over major plans. The Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, Han. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

Attending Committee Members Departed from the Capital Separately

(Nanjing) After the Second Plenary Session closed on the 14th, Song Ziwen flew to Shanghai at noon. Liu Yazi and others returned to Shanghai in the afternoon. Zhang Zhiben, Sun Jingya, Xue Dubi, Yang Hu, Pan Gongzhan, He Shizhen, Cai Yuanpei, and others returned to Shanghai on the night of the 14th. Guangdong Central Committee members Deng Qingyang, Yang Xixu, and five other committee members went to Shanghai on the evening of the 15th. The remaining committee members, such as the chairmen of various provinces Huang Shaoxiong, Xu Yongchang, Shang Zhen, and others, will return to their posts within days. (Special dispatch from the 14th)

Overseas Chinese Compatriots and the Second Plenary Session

(Nanjing) The Secretariat of the Second Plenary Session recently received a telegram from more than ten groups, including the Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce in the Philippines, saying: "National affairs are difficult and foreign insults are imminent. Now that leaders from all parties are gathering together to discuss national affairs, the rise and fall, safety and danger are of great importance. Overseas Chinese have heard of this and deeply look forward to it. The country is in a time of crisis, and what the people hope from you is to remove prejudices, be open and honest with each other, adhere to the original intention of sincere unity, and determine the strategy of resisting the enemy and saving the country. As for military affairs and finance, we should strive for unity, so as to unify the front and jointly face the national crisis. It is a matter of life and death, and we hope that you will earnestly consider it. Our association and others are in a foreign country, but our hearts are with the motherland. Upholding the duty of every man to do his part, we cannot remain silent. We earnestly appeal and hope that you will understand. We are anxiously looking forward to your reply." Signed, The Manila Chinese Chamber of Commerce in the Philippines and eleven other groups. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

Kong Xiangxi Invites Zhang Xueliang and Others to a Banquet

(Nanjing) Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi invited more than 20 Central Committee members, including Zhang Xueliang, Deng Qingyang, Huang Linshu, Li Wenfan, Yang Yongtai, Liu Zhenhua, Yang Hu, He Chengjun, Huang Shaoxiong, Liu Zhi, Shang Zhen, Xu Yongchang, Chen Cheng, Zhang Zhiben, Sun Jingya, He Shizhen, and others to a tea party at his private residence in Gaoloumen on the afternoon of the 14th. Kong and Vice Ministers Xu and Zou received the guests separately. (Special dispatch from the 14th)

(Nanjing) Judicial Yuan President Ju Zheng, Tan Zhen, Wang Yongbin, Jiao Yitang, Mao Zuquan, and others hosted a banquet for more than 60 Central Committee members, including Tang Shaoyi, Wang Chonghui, Sun Ke, Feng Yuxiang, Yu Youren, Yang Yongtai, Cui Guangxiu, and others at the Zhongshan Cultural Education Center on the evening of the 14th. (Special dispatch from the 14th)

Our Country Cancels Economic Sanctions Against Italy; The Executive Yuan Orders the Ministry of Finance to Telegraph Compliance

(Nanjing) The League of Nations General Assembly has resolved that economic sanctions against Italy will be lifted from 0:00 on July 15th. To take consistent action with the League of Nations, the Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Finance on the 14th to immediately telegraph the relevant agencies to comply with the cancellation. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 14th)

Current Commentary

The Conclusion of the Second Plenary Session

— Gao

The Fifth Second Plenary Session, after three general meetings, was declared closed yesterday. The major cases of current importance have been mostly discussed and completed. The most noteworthy resolutions, such as the organization of the National Defense Conference, the abolition of the two southwestern organizations, and the change of the pacification director of Guangdong Province, are all issues that we believe are not easy to handle. However, they were able to consider things carefully within the appropriate limits and take everything into account. The result of this plenary session cannot be said to be without considerable success.

At the beginning of the opening of the plenary session, what we were most concerned about was the difficulty in dealing with the Guangdong-Guangxi issue. The slogans advocated by Guangdong and Guangxi were to promote resistance to foreign aggression, the central government's prerequisite steps were to unify military orders, and the people's only request was to eliminate civil war. Although there is no conflict of interest in the grand plan of national salvation, the actual implementation showed a situation of division. Guangdong and Guangxi took advantage of the name of resisting the enemy and evolved into a fact of independent action. In order to maintain its prestige, the central government could not avoid imposing considerable sanctions. Once the mood was lost, war would break out. Therefore, at that time, we exhausted our wisdom and hoped that the authorities would promote cooperation with the greatest tolerance. Fortunately, the efforts of the gentlemen of the General Assembly have yielded such a result. The organization of the National Defense Conference is the first step in accommodating the opinions of the military personnel of Guangdong and Guangxi. The abolition of the two southwestern organizations is the precursor to the unification of power. The change of the pacification director of Guangdong Province is to take into account the prestige of the central government. At the same time, Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, and others were given good positions to maintain the status quo. Chen Jitang, who was dismissed, was also given a seat as a member of the National Defense Conference to avoid embarrassment, so as to eliminate subjective emotions and promote sincere unity. Such a stable arrangement should be understood by all parties, and we hope that the fear that has filled our hearts for months will be dispelled.

The joint decision on the major plan of resisting foreign aggression is also one of the things we have been eagerly looking forward to at the General Assembly. Since Foreign Minister Zhang announced the diplomatic process of the past six months at the General Assembly and Chairman Chiang reported the steps to save the country and resist foreign aggression, both recognized that the current diplomatic path has not yet reached the final juncture. Chiang also clearly showed the limits of his tolerance and the time when he could not tolerate it. This shows that the central government has never been without careful planning for the major plan of resisting foreign aggression. In the future, the unified situation will be formed, and the National Defense Conference will begin. For the adjustment of the entire diplomacy, it will be able to use concentrated strength as a solid backing. Looking at the figures contained in the members of the National Defense, they are either important figures in various aspects or the top choices for defense. They should be able to sharpen their skills and write their hearts and minds, so as to jointly plan a calm and unified pace and prepare for extraordinary and necessary responses. The pivot of national survival has reached the most critical stage. Can the whole country not be careful and strive to move forward?

Guangdong Designates Northeast River as Special Wartime Martial Law Zone; Guangzhou Implements General Martial Law; Guangdong Troops Withdraw Completely from Yuechang and Pingshi; Guangxi Troops Land and Transfer to North River; Situation in Shaoguan Gradually Becomes Serious; Deng Longguang Resigns, Cai Tingkai Declares He Will No Longer Participate

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang received a telegram from the central government dismissing him on the evening of the 13th. He immediately convened a military conference. Guangzhou immediately implemented general martial law that evening and declared the Northeast River as a special wartime martial law zone. The two divisions of Wu Jianxiong and Huang Zhiwen were withdrawn from Yuechang and Pingshi and redeployed to Yingde and Maba for defense. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) Two torpedo boats that escaped from Guangdong left Hong Kong at 4:00 PM on the 14th to head to Xiamen to await orders. It is rumored that all captains of ships gathered in the Pearl River have been placed under surveillance by Chen to prevent further escapes. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) The Qingxi Railway Bridge on the Guangdong Railway was repaired on the 14th and reopened to traffic on the 15th. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) Deng Longguang, the commander of the 9th Division, resigned from his post to Chen Jitang and arrived in Hong Kong on the evening of the 13th. The Political Council decided on the 14th to extend the term of the Guangdong Provincial Senators for another year and additionally appointed Li Yukun as a pacification commissioner in the Shantou region. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) The Guangxi troops of Wang Zanbin and Zhou Zuhan, two divisions, boarded ships from Wuzhou on the 9th and entered Guangdong. They landed in Sanshui and transferred to the North River. Wang's division arrived in Shixing on the 13th, and Zhou's division arrived in Qingyuan on the 14th for defense deployment. Their salaries are paid by Guangdong and they are under the command of one group army. Wang Dinghua's regiment was reorganized into the Second Independent Brigade and stationed in Shaoguan after arriving from Hainan. Guo Jiheng, the adjutant-general of the 6th Guangdong Division, was detained by Zhang Da in Shaoguan and sent to the provincial capital. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) Cai Tingkai declared on the 14th that Chen Jitang's cause was lost and he had decided to no longer participate. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) Wang Zanbin is scheduled to fly to Guangdong on the 15th to meet with Chen and Li. In order to amass a large force, Chen decided to further shorten the defense line and withdraw the two armies in Shaoguan and Chen Zhang's division from Dakengkou southward, with Yingde as the first, Yuantan the second, and Juntian the third defense lines. The Guangdong Railway Bureau dispatched vehicles to Shaoguan on the 14th to transport troops southward. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) A telephone call from Shaoguan on the morning of the 14th reported that Mo Xide's division of the First Army from southern Jiangxi returned to Guangdong and arrived in Nanxiong and Shixing, with the vanguard only thirty li away from Shaoguan. The two divisions of Ye Zhao and Zhang Ruigui continued to advance. The Guangdong troops in Yuechang and Pingshi were completely withdrawn. The three divisions of Li Zhenliang, Chen Zhang, and Wu Jianxiong departed from Shaoguan on the evening of the 14th and returned to Juntian. Li Xiangen, due to the urgency of the Guangdong Railway transportation, sent a telegram urging all employees to be diligent and cautious in their work. The people of Guangdong mostly oppose the entry of Guangxi troops into Guangdong and are still negotiating. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) Starting on the evening of the 13th, mines were laid at the Humen Fortress, and martial law was declared. Subsequently, all Guangdong ships leaving the port must be notified in advance by headquarters. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) It is rumored that a part of Yan Yingyu's division in Guangdong is now surrendering to Fujian. The authorities are requesting instructions on how to handle the situation. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) Today, the Political Committee appointed Li Yukun as a Pacification Commissioner for the Shantou region. It has just been confirmed that Guangdong and Guangxi are now organizing a joint anti-Japanese army, with Chen Jitang as the commander-in-chief and Li Zongren as the deputy commander-in-chief. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(Hong Kong) The Guangdong Third Army under Li Yangjing, originally stationed around the Xiaobei River, was ordered in the past two days to concentrate in Yingde. The rear defense was taken over by the two Guangxi divisions of Zhou Zuhan and Wang Zanbin. The Guangdong First Army, First Division (Mo Xide) and Second Division (Ye Zhao), actively advanced towards Shaoguan and Yingde. The situation in Shaoguan is very serious. (China United Press dispatch on the 14th)

(Guangzhou) The troops under Yu Hanmou, the newly appointed commander-in-chief of the Guangdong Army and the Pacification Commissioner of Guangdong Province, are preparing to move out today to implement the orders of the Central Executive Committee. Their vanguard has reached Pingshi, fifteen miles from the Jiangxi border. Chen Jitang's army, in order to shorten the battle line, has withdrawn to Shaoguan, seventy-five miles to the southwest. This army is composed of the Guangdong Second Army under Zhang Da, which recently concentrated in Yuechang, and other troops that recently invaded Hunan Province. News of the outbreak of war on the front line has been received here, but it has not yet been confirmed. Although the claim that the Guangxi army has arrived in Guangzhou and is heading to the North River area, according to Chen Jitang and Li Zongren's arrangements, has been denied, everyone believes it to be true. Guangzhou and its suburbs are currently stepping up defenses. The Southwest Political Committee held a meeting today to discuss the overall situation, which lasted for three hours. The atmosphere throughout the city is very serious, but the people remain calm. The most significant aspect is the continued stability of the financial situation, and the Guangdong currency has risen. The Customs Political Committee is holding a meeting.

Yu Hanmou Takes Office in Dayu; Circular Telegram Believes the Safety of Guangdong Lies Solely on Chen; Two Elders from the Capital Will Go to Guangdong in a Private Capacity to Persuade Chen

(Nanjing) Yu Hanmou flew to Jiangxi and has transferred to the front line. He made the military decision to take up the posts of Pacification Commissioner of Guangdong, Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Route Army, and Commander of the First Army. After meeting with the division commanders on the border, he is preparing to return to Guangzhou as a pioneer in resolving the current situation. Many of Chen Jitang's troops have expressed their obedience to the central government. Commissioners familiar with the Guangdong situation believe that Chen has been widely abandoned and cannot achieve anything. Even if he is ignorant of the greater good and stubbornly refuses to come to his senses, there will definitely not be any major disturbances. Although no formal telegrams from Li Zongren and Bai Chongxi have arrived in the capital, their tone in private telegrams to central committee members here is much more conciliatory. The central government, in order to rectify discipline and consider the deep comradeship, friendship, and kindness, has made a concrete decision. However, due to the urgency of the overall situation, the authorities will carefully consider the wording of the declaration before it is issued. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

The Guangdong members of the Central Committee attending the meeting plan to recommend two elders to go south in a private capacity to persuade Chen Jitang to consider the overall situation and return military and political power to the central government. The two elders are considering it, and it has not yet been decided when they will depart. (Dispatch on the 14th)

(Nanjing) He Jian, Chairman of Hunan Province, visited Chairman Lin and military authorities on the 14th. He stated that the affairs of Guangdong and Guangxi had been resolved by the plenary session, but the issue of Chen Jitang's personal advancement and retreat had not yet been settled. He specifically sent a telegram to Chen, asking him to abide by the central government's orders, consolidate the safety of the party and the country, and retire when he sees the opportunity. (Dispatch on the 14th)

Telegram from Dayu: To Chairman Lin of the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government, Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission, Vice Chairmen Yan and Feng, Premier Jiang of the Executive Yuan, the ministers and vice ministers of the various Yuan, the chairmen and directors of the various ministries and commissions, the party headquarters, provincial and municipal governments, pacification commissioners, commanders-in-chief, commanders, army and division commanders, commanders, various agencies, courts, and newspapers of each province and city: On the 12th of this month, I received an appointment from the Military Affairs Commission of the National Government, specially appointing Yu Hanmou as Pacification Commissioner of Guangzhou and Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Route Army. I respectfully took the oath of office at Dayu on the 14th. Aware of my limited talents, I have been entrusted with a heavy responsibility. Now that the country's affairs are unsettled, how dare I claim credit? I can only vow to be loyal and repay the Party and the country. However, there is something I cannot refrain from saying about the Guangdong situation. In recent years, foreign troubles have been pressing daily. Without resisting aggression, we cannot seek survival. Without unification, we cannot resist aggression. The central government's efforts to achieve peaceful unification are truly a crucial plan to concentrate forces to save the country. I, Hanmou, formerly led troops into Jiangxi, vowing to suppress the communists, resist Japan, and achieve peaceful unification to save the country. In all my actions, I have dared not deviate. Unfortunately, at a time when our Guangdong is facing national crisis, it suddenly took up arms, secretly colluded with foreign bandits, invaded neighboring provinces, and launched a civil war, undermining unification. The facts are evident and cannot be denied. My loyal words were rejected, and my benevolence and wisdom were exhausted. Therefore, I flew to the capital to request instructions, hoping to salvage the situation. I advocated obeying the central government, ceasing fighting, and resisting aggression, which should be understood by the people of the country. Reflecting on my life in the military, I have always been content with simplicity. I have no desire for power and rights. However, the survival of the country and the nation cannot be ignored. Therefore, I resolutely took office to fulfill my original intention. This sincere heart can be attested by Heaven and Earth. Today, the safety of the Guangdong situation rests solely on Bo Gong's (Chen Jitang's) shoulders. I urge him to obey the central government, release his troops and go to the capital to assist in important matters. Then peaceful unification can be achieved immediately, and the great plan to resist aggression will not be disrupted. The comrades in Guangdong are mostly stirred up. The central government is generous and treats everyone equally, without discrimination. They should be able to understand this heart and advocate justice together. Resisting aggression and seeking survival depends on this. I respectfully offer my sincere heart and plead my true feelings. I await your clear instructions.

National Defense Conference Regulations; The Full Text Contains Eight Articles; Approved for Implementation

(Nanjing) The National Defense Conference Regulations were passed by the Second Plenary Session of the Second Central Committee on the 13th and have now been promulgated. The original text is as follows:

Article 1: In order to reorganize national defense, a National Defense Conference is specially established to discuss national defense policies and important issues related to national defense.

Article 2: The National Defense Conference shall be composed of the following members: 1. Chairman: Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission; Vice Chairman: Premier of the Executive Yuan; 2. Members: (1) Heads of central military organs, two vice chairmen of the Military Affairs Commission, Chief of General Staff, President of the Military Advisory Council, Director General of Training, Chairman of the Aviation Committee; (2) Relevant ministers of the Executive Yuan (Ministers of Military Affairs, Navy, Finance, Foreign Affairs, Transportation, Railways, etc.); (3) Military and political leaders specifically appointed by the central government.

Article 3: The National Defense Conference shall deliberate on the following matters: 1. National defense policy; 2. National defense foreign policy; 3. Matters concerning the cooperation between national defense undertakings and national government affairs; 4. Matters concerning the handling of national defense emergencies; 5. Matters concerning national mobilization; 6. All organizations concerning wartime; 7. Other important matters related to national defense.

Article 4: The National Defense Conference shall be convened by the Chairman and shall hold a general meeting once a year. When necessary, extraordinary meetings may be convened.

Article 5: The resolutions of the National Defense Conference shall be submitted by the Chairman to the central government and handed over to the competent Yuan and Ministry for execution by order of the National Government.

Article 6: Each session of the National Defense Conference shall be limited to one week. If necessary, it may be extended.

Article 7: The National Defense Conference shall establish a secretariat. The Chief of the Secretariat shall be concurrently held by the Chief of General Staff. There shall be two Deputy Chiefs, who shall be concurrently held by the Deputy Director of the Office of the Military Affairs Commission. Its organization shall be determined separately.

Article 8: These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Central Executive Committee. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 14th)

(Nanjing) The National Government ordered on the 14th that Chiang Kai-shek be specially appointed as Chairman of the National Defense Conference. This order appointed Chiang Kai-shek as Vice Chairman of the National Defense Conference. This order appointed Yan Xishan, Feng Yuxiang, Cheng Qian, Zhu Peide, Tang Shengzhi, and Chen Diaoyuan as members of the National Defense Conference. This order appointed Kong Xiangxi, He Yingqin, Chen Shaokuan, Zhang Qun, Zhang Jia'ao, and Yu Feipeng as members of the National Defense Conference. This order appointed Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, Chen Jitang, Liu Zhi, Zhang Xueliang, Song Zheyuan, Han Fuqu, He Chengjun, Gu Zhutong, Liu Xiang, Long Yun, He Jian, Jiang Dingwen, Yang Hucheng, Zhu Shaoliang, Xu Yongchang, Fu Zuoyi, and Yu Hanmou as members of the National Defense Conference.

Chen became enraged and threatened to close the bank to force the withdrawal of customs revenue. The bank authorities refused based on reason and urgently telegraphed the head office for instructions. The reporter, believing that this matter concerned national finance, specifically visited a responsible official of the Ministry of Finance to inquire about the truth. According to the official, the ministry had also received reports of this matter. The Guangzhou branch of the Bank of China's refusal to Chen Jitang's forced withdrawal of customs revenue deposits, in accordance with banking regulations, was indeed an appropriate measure. If, unfortunately, this truly leads to Chen Jitang closing the bank, the government will devise other countermeasures to maintain the safety of the financial sector. Central Commemoration Week: Chairman Chiang's Report on Unification to Save the Nation

1. The foundation of diplomacy lies entirely in domestic affairs; therefore, the unification of domestic affairs is the key to resisting foreign aggression.

2. The Central Government, regarding the Guangdong and Guangxi incident, has consistently maintained a spirit of magnanimity, using political means and peaceful methods to resolve everything.

3. The unification of political and military orders is a fundamental requirement for dealing with foreign countries.

4. The Central Government can never abandon the pacification of internal disorder due to the severity of foreign troubles.

5. In resolving domestic problems, both reason and sentiment must be taken into account, but right and wrong, obedience and disobedience, must also be clearly distinguished.

6. The revolutionary government is determined to fight to the end amidst attacks from both within and without, from beginning to end.

(Nanjing) (Continued from yesterday) Since September 18th, the consistent policy of the Central Government has been "internal pacification first, external resistance second." It is believed that if the interior is not secure, not only can there be no external resistance, but even the word "diplomacy" cannot be discussed. From this, it can be seen that although the important cases discussed in this plenary meeting include both domestic and foreign affairs, they are actually only a domestic issue. I have always believed that the foundation of diplomacy lies entirely in domestic affairs. As long as domestic problems can be properly resolved, diplomatic problems can naturally be satisfactorily resolved. Everyone must understand that if our domestic affairs can truly be unified and the foundation of the country can be stabilized, any powerful country in the world will respect and fear us. As long as we are truly unified, no one will dare to be our enemy. Therefore, the matters discussed in this meeting should especially focus on resolving domestic problems to stabilize the foundation of the country, realize our Three Principles of the People, and complete the task of revolutionary nation-building. Speaking of domestic affairs, both the central and local governments are now responsible by comrades of our party. Therefore, all domestic instability and disunity are the result of the failure of party comrades to unite or even disputes. It can never be blamed on the general public who love the country. Now, if we want to unify and stabilize domestic affairs, we must first resolve internal party disputes. To resolve this dispute, we should, of course, handle everything in accordance with party discipline and national law. However, the revolutionary spirit of our party is based on the eight virtues of "loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, harmony, and peace." Regardless of any internal or external problem, we have always sought proper solutions in the spirit of "trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace," which is especially important internally. In the past, Chen Jiongming revolted in Guangzhou, attacking the presidential palace with artillery and machine guns, trying to kill the premier. However, the premier still tolerated him with a benevolent spirit. In the end, as long as Chen Jiongming could repent and reform, he would not be held responsible for the past. The premier's great spirit is truly a revolutionary model for all our party comrades. Now everyone is very concerned about the Guangdong and Guangxi incident. If this matter is purely based on the country's laws and disciplines, there is naturally no room for indulgence or tolerance. However, the central government has always been as tolerant as possible, based on trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace, and has never given up political means and peaceful methods to resolve the issue. It is also based on the premier's magnanimous spirit as the foundation for our handling of the incident. Now, several comrades in Guangdong and Guangxi who are responsible for military affairs have a slogan, "Military orders can only be unified under the banner of resisting Japan." They use the unification of Germany after the Franco-Prussian War in 1871 as an example, saying that only after winning against a foreign country can unification be completed. They naturally think that this slogan and this statement are very reasonable, but they don't know that they are completely wrong. We can also know that Germany took the customs union of seventeen states in 1834 as an opportunity, and due to the result of the industrial revolution and Bismarck's hard work. Although the country was composed of many federations, the unification of political and military orders had gradually been completed before the war against France. Only by unifying political and military orders first can France be defeated, not by defeating France and then unifying political and military orders. From this, we can see that the unification of military and political orders is a fundamental requirement for foreign resistance. Without unified military and political orders, there can be absolutely no external resistance. Several military authorities in Guangdong and Guangxi, because they do not understand this principle, and at the same time have not thoroughly studied and understood the realistic environment of the country and the world situation, and have not deeply understood our revolutionary position, have taken many wrong actions, creating the current mess. They do not cherish the history of the revolution, which is very painful. However, the party and the country have been greatly affected by this, and the tens of millions of compatriots in Guangdong and Guangxi, the source of our revolution, have especially suffered endless pain. Now that their incident is less than two months old, the people of Guangdong and Guangxi are already living in dire straits. Local soldiers are so reckless in their actions, causing trouble to the country. This is something that all comrades of our party, especially I, who is in charge of military affairs in the central government, cannot but take responsibility for self-reflection. I sincerely believe that my credibility has not been established, causing the country and the people to be in sorrow and pain, and adding another layer of danger and shock. Asking myself, I really feel very sorry and sad. Now that the facts have evolved to this point, on the one hand, we must of course always be based on trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace, and in the spirit of the premier's magnanimity, use all peaceful and political means, hoping that the military authorities in Guangdong and Guangxi can repent and reform, so that the situation can be stabilized again, and the country can have the strength to deal with foreign countries. But on the other hand, we must also have the determination and courage to rectify discipline and maintain unity, take responsibility to quell disorder and stabilize changes, and never abandon the work of quelling internal disorder due to the severity of foreign troubles. We must never, because of concerns about the oppression of foreign troubles, listen to a few local soldiers destroying discipline and acting freely, and everything is done in a perfunctory manner. Everyone must understand that, in terms of revolutionary strategy, precisely because of the oppression of foreign enemies, the central government must first thoroughly eliminate internal disorder. Otherwise, general traitors and bandits will want to take advantage of the enemy, and the country will have no hope of stability and revival. When foreign troubles are serious, if there are traitors and bandits who take advantage of the enemy, the central government should disregard everything and thoroughly clarify the situation in order to achieve the complete success of internal pacification and consolidate the foundation of external resistance. If we look ahead and behind, are timid and fearful, and are afraid of the constraints and interference of foreign forces, and therefore do not dare to rectify domestic affairs, then we will have no way to complete the work of building the country and defending against foreign insults. Then we will no longer be able to talk about revolution. If we want to revolutionize, we cannot be afraid of foreign troubles. If we revolutionaries are afraid of the oppression of imperialists, then we cannot revolutionize at all. For example, fifteen years ago, there were imperialist forces everywhere under our arms in Guangzhou. If we want to look ahead and behind, can we still send troops to the Northern Expedition? Since the revolutionary army vowed to launch the Northern Expedition, it was determined to fight to the end with all warlords and red bandits and traitors who took advantage of the enemy, and all anti-revolutionary elements who had no concept of the country, amidst attacks from both within and without. This spirit of the revolutionary army has always been consistent and fully demonstrated at any time and any place. Now, the reason why we want to use peaceful political methods to resolve domestic problems is absolutely not because of fear of foreign troubles and fear of the danger of being attacked from both within and without, but entirely for the sake of the historical feelings between comrades and the relationship of unity and concentrated strength. In other words, it is for the sake of cherishing the strength of the country, maintaining internal integrity, and demanding the overall awareness and unity, so that everyone can work together in the future to jointly resist foreign insults and revive the country's great cause. Therefore, we must take the spirit of the premier's all-encompassing spirit as our spirit and use peaceful methods as much as possible to resolve the issue, in order to comfort our premier and the spirits of the dead comrades in heaven. Recently, all comrades of the central government, of course, have the same mind and the same reason for solving domestic problems. They have always adhered to the spirit of trustworthiness, righteousness, peace, and all-encompassing spirit, and used peaceful political methods to deal with all chaos. But everyone must know that if a country wants to exist independently in the world, it must maintain the essential elements of building a country in spirit and the discipline of unifying domestic power. If the spirit is not rectified and discipline is not established, the country will become an unorganized and lifeless state. In short, it will not become a country. No matter when, no matter what country, they will want to invade and oppress us, and they will not treat us Chinese as citizens with independent personality. They will treat us Chinese as slaves of a conquered country. If we are only afraid of foreign troubles and disregard discipline, causing the country to lose its spirit, then no matter how big the country is or how many people there are, it will eventually perish. Therefore, when we deal with domestic problems, we must, of course, take both sentiment and reason into consideration, and we cannot completely abandon national law and discipline. Therefore, in sentiment and reason, we must also distinguish between right and wrong, and understand obedience and disobedience. If right and wrong are not distinguished, and obedience and disobedience are not understood, then discipline will not be established, and the country will inevitably perish with it. Therefore, now, when we solve domestic problems, historical prestige and emotion cannot be ignored, and right and wrong, obedience and disobedience, must not be unclear. I hope that all comrades of the central government, in the plenary meeting, will use the spirit of trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace, and the principle of taking both sentiment and reason into account, to study a proper solution to domestic problems, so that our country will forever eliminate the roots of betrayal and division, and achieve true and thorough unity, in order to save the country from danger. This is a bit of my opinion and prestige on state affairs, and I specially offer it to all comrades of the central government for your reference when discussing matters at the meeting. (Central News Agency telegram on the 13th)

Local Products and Goods: Import License Required

(Nanjing) In order to prevent smuggling, the Ministry of Finance specially stipulated, in accordance with the Interim Regulations on Inspecting the Transportation and Sale of Imported Goods, that the goods to be inspected include artificial silk, sugar, and more than 20 other items. However, some of them are local products and goods, and there is no import tax certificate for verification. Customs inspection is quite difficult. Now, after considering the actual needs, it is planned to formulate a license for the transportation and sale of imported local products and a distribution license for assistance. All types of goods that are stipulated above to be inspected, if they are local products, should apply for a license for the transportation and sale of local products and a distribution license with solid certification from the local Chamber of Commerce or trade association before they can be shipped. This method can be announced and implemented within days. (Central News Agency telegram on the 14th)

It is divided into special, first-class, and second-class. Special is one yuan, first-class is six jiao, and second-class is two jiao. (Special dispatch on the 14th)

(2) According to the captured bandits, the remnants of the bandits are very short of ammunition. The rifles are all 6.5 caliber, and the machine guns are all 7.9 caliber. The 7.9 caliber rifle ammunition has been transferred to machine guns and is secretly buried underground in northern Shaanxi, fearing that it will be captured by our army. British Company Produces Humiliating Film; Chargé d'Affaires in Britain Lodges a Protest

(London) Gaumont British Picture Corporation is currently producing a film entitled "Ohms." One scene depicts British soldiers crossing a river to attack Chinese pirates. The pirates are riding horses, wearing straw hats, and carrying old-fashioned rifles, charging at the British soldiers. As they advance, they yell like demons. The Chinese Minister to Britain, Guo Taiqi, is currently not in London, so Chargé d'Affaires Dr. Chen Weicheng has requested the company to remove this scene. According to Dr. Chen's interview with Reuters today, "I often protest to film companies, and with their understanding, they are always accommodating. You must know that besides bandits, there are many good things in China. Recently, Chinese students noticed the Chinese opium den in Madame Tussaud's Wax Museum. After I sent a letter to the museum's director, it was immediately removed. I hope the Gaumont British Picture Corporation can refer to their Chinese pirates as oriental outlaws."
