Anglo-Egyptian Treaty Negotiations Last Four Months; Military Clauses Largely Compromised; In the Form of Alliance and Friendship; Sudan Issue Still to Be Discussed

(London) According to well-informed sources, the military clauses of the Anglo-Egyptian treaty currently under discussion have not yet been finalized, but major points have been compromised. These clauses are currently being drafted. The final military clauses will be discussed based on other parts of the agreement, such as those concerning Sudan and the rights enjoyed by foreign communities. It is believed that progress has been made on the following points: (1) The agreement will be in the form of alliance and friendship; (2) British troops will withdraw from Cairo and relocate to Ismailia; (3) Egypt will ultimately be responsible for the national defense and the defense of the Suez Canal, but the number of British troops will only be reduced after the Egyptian army is adequately strengthened; (4) Egypt must build a network of military highways so that troops can be quickly deployed to the east and west; (5) The British Air Force will be greatly increased, and new airfields will be built in Abu Agga and Ismailia; (6) An important British naval base will be established in Alexandria, with Britain paying land rent. A larger army base will also be established. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Britain Determines Not to Cancel the Mediterranean Mutual Assistance Pact; Baldwin's Statement in the House of Commons

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin stated in the House of Commons today that Britain will currently refuse to abolish the Mediterranean Mutual Assistance Pact signed last year with Turkey, Greece, and Yugoslavia. Even if Italian Prime Minister Mussolini insists on abolishing it, Britain will not change its attitude. (National Telegram on the 13th)

British Government Announces Civil Supplementary Budget; Intends to Use £850,000 to Manufacture a Large Number of Gas Masks

(London) A civil supplementary budget of £4 million was released today, including £857,000 to manufacture a huge number of gas masks. It was also resolved that these masks should not be issued unless absolutely necessary, but should be stored in various departments throughout the country for convenience. The Prime Minister's center point, and will invite citizens to automatically practice using it. The budget also includes an additional 100,000 pounds for secret affairs. The expenses for the revised budget in 1936 totaled 350,000 pounds. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Straits Defenses Issue; Significant Progress in Montreux Conference; Disputed Points Virtually Agreed Upon; Final Revision of New Convention's Wording; Formal Signing Expected by End of This Week

Montreux: The disputed points of the Dardanelles Straits Conference have been virtually agreed upon. A plenary session will be held tomorrow. At the final plenary session around the end of this week, a new convention may be signed. The drafting committee of the new convention will meet tonight to finalize the wording of each clause in the treaty. It is heard that the provisions stipulate that in the event of a war in which Turkey maintains neutrality, the warships of all belligerent countries shall not pass through the Dardanelles Straits, except for obligations under the League of Nations. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

Anglo-Russian Disputes; Seeking Compromise Solutions; French Representatives Mediate

Montreux: Representatives from various countries at the Montreux Conference are seeking compromise solutions on the points of dispute between Britain and Russia. A plenary session is scheduled to be held at 4 p.m. today, hoping to reach a compromise. Regarding the Russian delegation's request that the country's Black Sea fleet be allowed to freely pass through the straits and enter the Mediterranean Sea, the British delegation is no longer firmly opposed. However, it has put forward three other proposals: (1) Adopting a reciprocal approach, that is, if Russian warships enter the Mediterranean Sea from the Black Sea, then countries not bordering the Black Sea should be allowed to send warships of equal tonnage into the Black Sea; (2) Britain still objects to the Russian proposal that warships of all countries be allowed to freely pass through the straits if they are fulfilling obligations under regional mutual assistance pacts. Regarding this point, the compromise proposal jointly put forward by the French and Turkish delegations may also be of no avail; (3) Regarding the issue of whether to abolish the Straits Commission, Turkey, Romania, and Greece all advocate abolishing it, while Britain and France advocate retaining it. However, Britain believes that this matter is not of great importance and will not hinder the progress of the negotiations. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Montreux: After the British delegation expressed its objections to the Russian delegation's proposal that warships of all countries be allowed to freely pass through the straits if they are fulfilling obligations under regional mutual assistance pacts, the French and Turkish delegations immediately jointly put forward a compromise proposal. Because the British delegation needs to consult with the government, it is not convenient to decide its attitude on its own. Therefore, the plenary session of the Montreux Conference, which was scheduled to be held this afternoon, is likely to be postponed. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Montreux: Well-informed sources have recently announced that the Russian and Turkish delegations attending the Montreux Conference have virtually no more differences of opinion. However, there are obvious differences of opinion between Britain and Russia regarding how to fulfill the obligations stipulated in the regional pact within the scope of the future new convention (namely, Article 23 of the British amendment). France is currently making every effort to mediate this. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Britain Agrees to Abolish the Straits Management Committee; Accommodating Turkey's Request

Montreux: The British representative to the Montreux Conference, Lountel, returned here this morning from London with new instructions. As is generally known, the new instructions are more moderate. Regarding the international committee managing the straits, Britain may accommodate Turkey's request and abolish it. Regarding the issue of the passage of Soviet warships through the Dardanelles Straits in wartime, a compromise solution will also be sought that is acceptable to the Soviet Union (that is, Article 16 of the British draft). The only thing it firmly opposes is the amendment proposed by Russia to Article 23 of the British draft (the content of which is that the Dardanelles and Bosphorus Straits must be closed in wartime, but all warships may freely pass through the straits to implement the various obligations contained in existing or future regional pacts). After Lountel arrived here this morning, in addition to meeting with the French representative Ponsot, he also had talks with Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov. In addition, French Chief Representative Poncet also arrived here at 6:30 p.m. today. Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü immediately went to visit and discuss the recent developments of the conference. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Austro-German Amity Agreement; Italian Prime Minister Strongly Supports; Contains a Secret Clause; Austrian Restoration Postponed to Three Years Later

(Rome) High-ranking officials today praised the newly established Austro-German agreement, the focal point of Prime Minister Li, and will invite citizens to automatically practice using it. The budget also includes an additional 100,000 pounds for secret affairs. The expenses for the revised budget in 1936 totaled 350,000 pounds. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th) Mussolini has actively supported the newly established Austro-German agreement, because its origin was actually the meeting between Mussolini and Austrian Chancellor Schuschnigg on June 5th. Mussolini not only approved the agreement, but also made many suggestions to Schuschnigg regarding its content. Therefore, although the agreement does not explicitly state the agreement of Germany and Italy, Germany knows that it has obtained Mussolini's strong support. (National Telegram on the 13th)

(Paris) A correspondent from the Paris Echo in London reports that, according to news from the capital of Yugoslavia, the agreement recently established between Germany and Austria contains a secret clause stipulating that the restoration of the Habsburg dynasty in Austria should be postponed until three years later. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(Vienna) The authorities have not yet begun to release Austrian National Socialists in accordance with the Austro-German agreement. It is said that it will take several weeks to examine the crimes of the National Socialists and distinguish between political prisoners and ordinary criminal offenders. Only political prisoners will be eligible for amnesty. (Reuters dispatch on the 13th)

Newspaper Commentary; Germany and Italy Echo Each Other

(Berlin) After the establishment of the Austro-German agreement, the newspapers here unanimously praised it, saying that it was a victory for German diplomacy, and that its international repercussions would be expected. The National Socialist Party's organ, the "Attack" newspaper, stated, "This agreement is a tool to deal with Soviet Russia, and the fate of the Locarno Conference has also been decided from now on." Political figures said that the current international problems are complex and complicated. The best way to solve them is for the countries concerned to directly conclude bilateral non-aggression pacts. This can be clearly demonstrated by the agreement recently established between Germany and Austria. Foreign Ministry officials stated that the Austro-German agreement does not mean the formation of a new group, and the agreements signed between Italy, Austria, and Hungary in 1934 and March of this year will continue to be in effect. In the future, Austria's policy will continue as before, and Germany will also continue to work hard to establish friendly relations with its neighboring countries. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

(Rome) After the establishment of the Austro-German agreement, the Giornale d'Italia here commented, stating that this agreement is actually a prelude to the transformation of Europe "outside the scope of the League of Nations," and this transformation should be based on new principles of international life, which are very different from democratic ideals. The Fascist Labor News stated, "Germany and Italy have the same needs. Their nations are both full of vitality, their political institutions are new and solid, and they have the same interests in maintaining European peace. Now, a new era of active cooperation between the two countries is about to begin. All countries that want to obtain the cooperation of Germany and Austria must first abandon their alliances with other countries." The alliances referred to by the newspaper are the mutual assistance agreement established by the countries along the Mediterranean coast, and the treaties signed by France with several small European countries. According to the newspaper, the former is a plan to resist Italy, while the latter is a tool to resist Germany. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Little Entente Countries Value the Consequences of the Austro-German Agreement; There Is Talk of Germany and Czechoslovakia Concluding a Non-Aggression Pact

Romanian Capital: After the establishment of the Austro-German agreement, political figures here have recently stated that the countries of the Little Entente, the Little Entente, and the Balkan Entente are carefully examining the consequences that this agreement may produce. It is also said that Romania has always believed that any solution to the Austrian issue should not be detrimental to Germany. This can be seen in the speech delivered by Foreign Minister Titulescu in the Chamber of Deputies on April 4, 1934. However, if Romania's rights are harmed by the Austro-German agreement, the government will definitely protect them with all its strength. According to Titulescu's speech, there is hope for a gradual improvement in the relations between Germany and Austria. This is in line with Romania's consistent policy of cooperation among the countries of Central Europe, but Romania will never participate in any economic or political organization that is aimed at Germany. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Yugoslav Capital: After the establishment of the Austro-German agreement, the Pravda newspaper here commented, stating, "The countries of Europe are maneuvering and forming groups, which is no different from the situation in 1914. However, the current alliance of Germany, Austria, and Italy is even stronger than the Triple Alliance of 1914. This is the difference." (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

(Berlin) After the establishment of the Austro-German agreement, Czech Minister Meisiel has been summoned back to his country. Some political figures here claim that it is possible that Germany and the Czech Republic will conclude a bilateral non-aggression pact. Meisiel's return to his country may be related to this matter, but it is not certain. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Czech Prime Minister Visits Austrian Capital

(Vienna) Czech Prime Minister Hodža recently arrived here in a private capacity. He has neither gone to the Czech embassy nor paid a courtesy visit to the Prime Minister's office. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Italian and German General Staffs Conclude Military Agreement; Negotiations in Rome Underway; Used to Offset the Franco-Italian Agreement

(Paris) Renowned journalist Madame Tabouis recently published a Rome dispatch in the L'Oeuvre newspaper, stating that a German military delegation arrived in Rome a few days ago to hold talks with Italian General Staff personnel and conclude an agreement. Regarding this, semi-official sources believe that General Gamlin of the French Army General Staff signed a military agreement with Italian General Staff personnel in Rome after the Franco-Italian Rome Agreement was concluded on January 7 of last year. Now that Italy has become closer to Germany, it wants to conclude a similar agreement with the German General Staff to offset the original military agreement between France and Italy. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

Italy Refuses to Participate in Locarno Conference; Britain, France, and Belgium Engage in Negotiations; Conference Will Be Postponed Indefinitely

Brussels: Prime Minister Zealand, in his capacity as convener of the Locarno Conference, sent a letter to Italy requesting that it send representatives to participate. The Italian government has already responded, refusing to participate. Foreign Minister Spaak met with British Ambassador Sir Walvey and French Ambassador Laroque this morning and showed them the Italian reply. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

(Rome) According to officials here, Italy must meet two conditions: (1) the abolition of the Mediterranean guarantee; (2) Germany must be invited to participate in the Locarno Conference. Only after these conditions are accepted by Britain, Belgium, and France will Italy be prepared to send representatives to attend the conference. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(London) Since the establishment of the Austro-German agreement, and Italy's refusal to participate in the Locarno Conference, the Belgian government is negotiating with Britain and France to prepare to postpone the holding of this conference. This has recently been confirmed by diplomatic sources. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

(London) The Locarno Powers Conference, scheduled to be held on July 22, is now increasingly likely to be postponed, or even postponed indefinitely. The new situation caused by recent diplomatic developments, and the attitude of Italy towards German participation in the conference, are all considered to be worth reconsidering. France's refusal to allow Germany to participate in the preliminary discussions of the conference may be resolved through talks through ordinary diplomatic channels, so that five countries will be present at the first official meeting of the Locarno Powers Conference. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(London) Regarding the date of the Locarno Conference, it is now learned that the British government's view is that the conference is only related to the powers of the Locarno Treaty. Since Germany has occupied the Rhineland, it is no longer a related country. Whether this view can be established depends on the outcome of the diplomatic exchange of views on the future of the conference currently being conducted by Britain, Belgium, and France. (Reuters dispatch on the 14th)

(London) Regarding the date of the Locarno Conference, well-informed sources here have recently stated that since Italy has refused to participate in this conference, the original date (July 22) may be postponed, but it is also uncertain. However, Foreign Secretary Eden is currently on vacation. He will return to the capital to resume his duties on Wednesday of this week. At that time, a decision can be made on the issue of whether the conference should be postponed. According to the opinions of political figures and parliamentarians, if the Locarno Conference is indeed postponed, the real reasons will be none other than the following two: (1) Since Italy and Germany are not participating, the participants in the conference will naturally be limited to Britain, France, and Belgium. This is not what Britain wants; (2) At the first meeting of the signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty in March of this year, an agreement was reached stipulating that if Germany remains unyielding, Britain and Italy will permanently guarantee the security of the borders of France and Belgium. If the conference is held abruptly now, the French and Belgian delegations will inevitably mention the aforementioned agreement. This is also something Britain does not want to hear. It is expected that the British government should follow two strategies in the future, namely (1) wait for Italy to change its attitude; (2) try to establish an understanding between Britain, France, Germany, Italy, and Belgium. Political figures mostly support the second strategy, believing that it is more advisable to start dealing with various European issues immediately, otherwise, it may be too late after the Austro-German agreement is truly implemented. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

British Foreign Secretary Resumes Duties

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden recently took a vacation to his home country for a few days of rest. His political health has now recovered, and he will return to the capital on Wednesday to resume his duties. (Havas dispatch on the 13th)

Romanian Foreign Minister Cancels Resignation Intention

Romanian Capital: Regarding the issue of Foreign Minister Titulescu's resignation, semi-official sources recently stated that after Titulescu suddenly returned from Montreux on the 9th of this month, he immediately held talks with the Prime Minister and obtained assurances that domestic issues must be adapted to foreign policy. Titulescu, because the situation has become clearer, has cancelled his intention to resign. (Havas dispatch on the 14th)

France Celebrates National Day: Military Parade Held, People's Front Makes Large-Scale March, Public Enthusiastic as Never Before

(Paris) President Lebrun and Premier Léon Blum held a military parade at 9:30 AM this morning to celebrate National Day, which lasted until 11:00 AM. The troops marched in formation, orderly and solemn. People from both the left and right wings cheered in unison to show their respect. Left-wingers wore a wild rose on their chest, while right-wingers wore tricolor badges for identification. Japanese Army Minister Eager to Implement New National Defense Plan, 800 Million Yuan Budget for Next Year, Still to Be Negotiated with Financial Authorities

(Tokyo) The new national defense plan drafted by the Japanese Ministry of the Army was submitted by Army Minister Terauchi to the consecutive national policy cabinet meetings held yesterday, requesting the understanding of the cabinet members. The Army Minister has high expectations for the plan, and insists that the items listed in the plan are all the minimum necessary facilities, and insists on implementing it no matter what. However, due to budgetary reasons, it needs to be negotiated with the financial authorities before a decision can be made. The content of the plan is divided into two parts in nature, the first part of the plan has an urgent nature, and must be fully implemented within five or six years from the Showa 12th fiscal year. The contents are (1) Expanding aviation and air defense facilities, with an initial temporary cost of approximately 600 million yuan and a regular cost of 200 million yuan. (2) Replenishing the troops stationed in Manchuria, with an initial temporary cost of 600 million yuan and a regular cost of 150 million yuan. The second part of the plan includes (1) Improving domestic military preparations, requiring an expenditure of 300 million yuan. (2) Preparing combat materials, requiring an expenditure of 100 million yuan, with a period of ten or twelve years, so that the domestic army can generally have excellent machinery and be fully modernized. Therefore, the total amount of the Army's budget for next year will be between 700 million and 800 million yuan. (Hualian News Agency, 14th)

Hebei Province's Financial Difficulties, Actively Planning Remedies, Province's Treasury Deficit of More Than Eight Million Yuan Annually, Compiling New Budget to Strive for Revenue and Expenditure Equilibrium, Jia Yuzhang Discusses Rectification Plan

Baoding Correspondence: Song Zheyuan, Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, instructed Jia Yuzhang, Director of the Finance Department, to carefully devise remedies for the province's treasury deficit, which amounts to more than eight million yuan annually. He also ordered that revenue and expenditure be balanced when compiling the new budget for the 25th year of the Republic and that no further deficits should occur. After receiving the instructions, Jia immediately invited Zhang Jiyong, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Wang Jingru, Director of the Department of Construction, Li Jinzao, Director of the Department of Education, Zhang Yunrong, Director of the Security Department, Li Xiantang, Director of the Police Department, and Wei Shuxiang, Secretary-General of the Provincial Government, to discuss ways to balance revenue and expenditure in the new budget for the 25th year of the Republic. Although many discussions were held, no concrete results were achieved. Ways to increase revenue were almost impossible to imagine, so everyone advocated finding ways to reduce expenditure. However, the province had previously implemented staff reductions, salary cuts, and the abolition of redundant agencies many times. This time, if a huge amount of more than eight million yuan is reduced again, it will be extremely difficult. Finally, the Finance Department drafted three principles for reduction and convened the directors of various departments to discuss everything for several days. Although there were many discussions, because the province's treasury deficit was too large, it was necessary to find a way to balance revenue and expenditure. Therefore, after many disputes, it was finally passed. The contents include: Abolishing unimportant agencies, Merging agencies with similar functions, and All public funds of the various departments will be issued at 70% of the original amount. As for which agencies to abolish or merge, the directors of each department still need to plan on their own and separately propose the items and amounts of abolition and merger within their own scope, and then jointly compile them to ensure that the total amount matches. At that time, the budget can be established. Now, the directors of each department feel that this matter is difficult because it is quite troublesome to reduce the budget by a huge amount of eight million yuan.

According to Jia Yuzhang, Director of the Finance Department, "The financial difficulties of this province urgently need to be broken, and the compilation of the new budget is also very troublesome. Although there are many difficulties in this matter, it is necessary to carefully find a solution due to practical needs. Regarding the compilation of the new budget, principles for reduction have already been drafted. As for the extent of the reduction and whether revenue and expenditure can be balanced, it is difficult to predict. I (Jia's self-reference) am now trying my best to seek budget revenue and expenditure balance under the principle of reduction for the province's financial difficulties. In addition, I also plan to formulate several plans to rectify the province's finances and actively implement them at the same time, so as to slightly supplement the province's treasury revenue. Currently, there are about three items being carried out: First, clearing up official property; Second, eliminating the malpractice of contract collection; Third, reforming the new tax collection system. The number of official properties in this province is very large, and the government has no accurate statistics. This time, all county magistrates are ordered to clear up the official properties in each county and at the same time handle the black land promotion, determine land sovereignty, which will not only slightly supplement the province's treasury revenue, but also prepare for future land reporting. As for eliminating the malpractice of contract collection, because the livestock slaughter tax and the two license taxes for wine and tobacco in this province for the 25th year of the Republic are all contracted by the county to select personnel, the intermediaries take the opportunity to engage in fraud during the bidding period, reporting more for less, colluding with contractors, and deliberately suppressing the contract amount in order to enrich themselves. The Finance Department has repeatedly investigated and found this to be true, and has ordered all county magistrates to be fair and abide by the rules, and has dispatched Inspector Ma Ronggui to Dingxing, Fangshan, Liangxiang, Yixian, Wanping, and other counties to conduct on-the-spot investigations to remove the barriers between the people and the government, which has yielded good results. Because Dingxing County's past monthly contracted amount was more than 7,000 yuan, this time Director Ma went and recruited contractors with more than 17,000 yuan. In this way, not only can the government slightly increase revenue, but the contractor can also be free of grievances, and the government and the people both feel convenient. This province has changed the collection system on July 1, implemented new tax rules, and established five district tax collection bureaus in Shijiazhuang, Baoding, Tianjin, Xingtai, and Shulu, which can reduce the operating expenses of the collection office by more than 200,000 yuan each year. All of these are ways for the authorities to raise funds and provide remedies for the financial difficulties of this province, and also to assist in completing the revenue and expenditure balance of the new budget." (July 11)

Sluggish Sales of Yellow Disaster Lottery Tickets - Public Welfare Charity Lottery Tickets to Be Discontinued -

Tianjin Correspondence: Hebei Province's Yellow Disaster Lottery Tickets were issued by Yu Xuezhong when he was in charge of the Hebei Provincial Government in the 23rd year of the Republic. They were issued until the twelfth issue, when they were ordered to be suspended and terminated. Last month, the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council commissioned the Tianjin Public Welfare Charity Lottery Tickets, which were initiated by Xiao Zhenying when he was the Mayor of Tianjin in May of this year, and were issued in Pingjin at the same time as the Yellow Disaster Lottery Tickets. Due to the impact of the recent economic downturn in North China, sales have been sluggish, and the income is barely enough to draw the lottery. The offices of the two lottery tickets felt that they could not support such sales, so they sent people to various provinces and cities to sell them in large quantities. Various places have consulted the Ministry of Finance one after another. The Ministry of Finance replied to various places in an instant, and at the same time ordered the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council and the Tianjin Municipal Government, because the two lottery tickets had not been approved, and the two lottery tickets have not been discontinued so far. They have expanded their publicity and even used strangely shaped parade advertisements to promote them, but the general public is unwilling to believe them and no one cares about them, which has led to increasingly sluggish lottery ticket sales. Regarding the Tianjin Public Welfare Charity Lottery Tickets, the office has invited the silver and money industry, the Chamber of Commerce, wealthy businessmen, and various groups to request assistance, and each industry is responsible for allocating sales externally, with a minimum of 10,000 yuan in bonuses per month, but all winners should be used as charity funds and should not be collected. In Tianjin, where commerce is declining day by day, most of them are affected by smuggling, and business is in a terrible state. Each month, they are responsible for 10,000 yuan in charity bonuses, and everyone is suffering. When the second phase of charity lottery tickets was issued, only 5,000 yuan was raised from commercial donations for the first time. The third phase of lottery tickets could not be promoted due to the Administrative Yuan's order to ban them. The office felt extremely panicked and recently planned to ask the municipal government to allocate sales to its subordinate agencies. All agencies expressed their opposition when they heard the news. Judging from the above situation, it is feared that the issuance will be stopped.

The Case of Urging and Pursuing Land Rent

Wu County, Xietang and other townships, for the problem of rent collection, farmers have repeatedly rioted due to rent problems, so the county government has successively dealt with them with administrative force, but the problem of rent collection is still ongoing. Recently, with the arrival of the busy farming season, the problem of rent collection has temporarily come to an end. The stubborn tenants detained by the Rent Collection Office have also been released one after another to return to farming. The rent collection offices in various townships have also been closed uniformly, but the color of the rent collection is extremely short, and the general landlords are quite disappointed. Although the rent collection has come to an end, each of the rent houses is still proceeding with the urging of rent through judicial procedures. A landlord, Zhou Chunlin, filed a lawsuit with the court against more than 60 households of tenants, including Ling Songfu, requesting a judgment to repay. The district court announced its judgment on the 14th, and the defendants Ling Songfu, Xu Lanqing, Zhu Yunlong, and other more than 60 households shall repay the outstanding land rent to the plaintiff separately, and the defendants shall bear the litigation costs. There are still a large number of tenants being sued by Qian Ding and others, and the district court is still summoning them. As for the problem of this year's land rent, it is quite important. County Chief Deng has specially proposed six principles and publicly solicits opinions in the newspaper on the 14th for reference.

Wuxi: Silk Factory Strike Ends

The female workers of 36 silk factories in this county, including Wufeng, Ruichang, Dingsheng, and Yongtai, went on a strike. It is learned that the county government convened representatives from labor and management, Ye Qiaoyun, Wang Baozhen, Xue Zukang, Hua Shaochun, and representatives from the General Labor Union, Sun Xiangfeng, representatives from the County Party Department, Li Xiping, and Chief of the Public Security Bureau, Chen Yuchu, to hold a mediation meeting on labor disputes at the silk factory. At that time, three points were decided: It is forbidden for such situations to occur again in the future, and the agitators will be cracked down on and punished. Work will resume on the 15th, and the factory should start work, and the workers should enter the factory and work with confidence. The conditions proposed by the workers will be resolved by the Party and government after work resumes. Each factory will send two representatives to work out a proper solution with the Industrial Union and the General Labor Union to the Party, government, and capital side. The county government will issue a notice of the decided points to inform everyone. At the same time, the Administrative Commissioner Zang Qifang, in addition to instructing County Chief Long to properly plan to solve the strike, also sent clerk Zhang Zhuoyu to investigate the Ruichang Wufeng Yongsheng and other factories. At that time, the staff of Yongsheng Factory reported the truth of the incident and said that the loss of all the factory's property and sundries was about 19,000 yuan. On the morning of the 14th, the female workers of each factory were still on strike. The Silk Factory Industry Union specially sent more than ten cadres to persuade the leaders of the workers in each factory to abide by the mediation principles of the county chief, to resume work uniformly on the 15th, and to inform all workers. Currently, the workers have decided to resume work on the morning of the 15th and wait for the Party and government to handle the matter fairly. The strike has come to an end.

In the Jiangsu Provincial Silkworm Experiment Field outside the west gate of this county, there are more than 100 male and female workers who work busily every day and rarely rest. Recently, the field suddenly extended working hours, abolished the Sunday system, and did not allow leave. More than 40 female workers felt quite painful about this. Yuyao: A Tragic Scene in Baisha Township

Hu Baotian, a resident of Baisha Township, Yuyao, was already sixty years old. His family was well-off. His wife had passed away early, leaving behind a daughter, Xiuying, who was of marriageable age. He recruited a tenant worker, Zhu Genzhang, as his son-in-law. The couple got along very well. However, fortunes changed suddenly, and good times didn't last. At the beginning of the month, Genzhang suddenly developed sores on his abdomen, which ulcerated severely. He groaned in bed, suffering intensely. Xiuying, deeply concerned for her husband, was misled by others who said that licking the rotten flesh could cure him. Therefore, disregarding the filth and poison, she frequently licked Genzhang's festering sores, causing the poison to attack her heart. Both of them died one after another. Baotian, facing such a tragedy in his later years, suffered a severe nervous shock. He cried out all day long. Unexpectedly, he also passed away due to phlegm obstruction. As a result, three corpses were left in the house, with no one to arrange the funeral. It is truly a tragic scene in the world.

After legal debate, the case was announced yesterday. The Zhenjiang-Huai'an route steamers of Yangzi, Litong, Zhentong, and Fuyun companies, as well as the freight transport steamers of the Ministry of Railways, and more than twenty tugboats, were detained in the river. Anxi Mining Exploration Concludes; Reserves Only 10 Million Tons; Japanese Technicians Already Dismissed; Future Mining Undecided

A correspondent from Xiamen reports that the Anxi Pantian coal mine, famous internationally, had the provincial government's Department of Construction organize the Anxi Iron Ore Exploration Project Office, appointing Zhao Xiujin as the director and hiring seventeen Japanese technicians from the South Manchuria Railway Company. Together with technicians from the Construction Department, they formed an exploration team to prospect in Anxi. They divided their work into four sections: railway, harbor, mining, and trial drilling. The railway, mining, and harbor work had been completed earlier. However, the trial drilling work required eight months because they needed to use a diamond drill to drill deep holes of 200 meters to extract iron sand, chemically test the mineral quality, and explore the reserves. Originally, a total of five holes were planned to be drilled. By June, three holes had been drilled. The mineral quality was still good, with an average iron content of over 50%. However, the quantity was not large. In June, banditry suddenly erupted in Anxi. Lü Zhenshan disrupted the mining area, occupied Taozhou, and once besieged Pantian. The Fifth Security Regiment defended for three days, relying on the Ninth Division Xie Brigade to lift the siege. As a result, the provincial government ordered the cessation of exploration. The remaining three Japanese trial drilling technicians were also dismissed. The borrowed Manchuria Railway drilling machine was transported to Jimei by fifteen trucks on the tenth and will arrive in Xiamen on the twelfth. Japanese chief technician Murakoshi Kikuzo also flew from Shanghai to Xiamen on the seventh to wait for inspection and recovery before being shipped to Dalian and returned to the South Manchuria Railway Company. According to Chen Gao, a technician from the Construction Department, "The Pantian mining area in Anxi is plagued by bandits, and the exploration work was hindered and suspended. However, although the trial drilling has not been completed in the past six months, the overall situation of the reserves has become clear. In terms of quantity, there are only about 10 million tons, not the huge 80 million tons. This April, Xie Jiarong, an expert from the Beijing Geological Institute, went to Pantian to survey the ore outcrops and also estimated 10 million tons. Whether to mine in the future is still undecided. However, transportation is difficult, and the investment in railways and ports is too large. The exploration cost this time is estimated at 120,000 to 130,000 yuan." It is said that the estimated cost of all equipment for the development of the Pantian mining area is 20 million yuan, but the quantity is only 10 million tons, so there may be no value in mining. Moreover, Fujian has no anthracite coal and cannot smelt steel. Even if it is mined, it will only be sold as iron sand to foreigners. (July 12)

A Good Story from the Southern Inspection Tour

— Special Correspondent Shi Ying

Lanxi Experimental County

Lanxi has the Qu Port (where rivers are called ports) and Wu Port, which converge outside the city to form the Lan Port, flowing downstream directly into the Qiantang River. Before the completion of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, it was the only route for counties such as Lishui and Quzhou, as well as the provinces of Fujian and Jiangxi, to go north to Shanghai and Hangzhou. It has always enjoyed the reputation of "a thoroughfare connecting seven provinces," holding the core of the commercial area in the mountainous region of eastern Zhejiang. The urban area gathers merchants from all over, and the market is very prosperous and lively. The lives of ordinary people are also relatively well-off. Since the construction of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Road and the subsequent opening of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, the commercial center has gradually shifted elsewhere. Jinhua, located in the middle of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Road, was originally Lanxi's neighbor. A branch road was built to give Jinhua an advantage in land transportation. There used to be a saying, "The Jinan government is small, but the Lanxi county is big." Now it has changed somewhat.

Lanxi and Jinhua are interconnected, with similar customs, and can be called "sister counties." For example, people only know that Jinhua's ham is delicious, but they don't know that most of the pigs are raised in Lanxi. Lanxi's fine dates are very sweet and sell well, but the date production area is far away in Jinhua. Lanxi's unique and interesting teahouses first created the fashion of "tea girls." The Jinhua tea gardens, not wanting to be left behind, have also begun to hire glamorous singers. In the past, officials who had served in the Jinhua government still wanted to serve as magistrates in Lanxi County. Conversely, those who had served in Lanxi County wanted to be transferred to the Jinhua government. The former was thinking about their pockets, while the latter was holding their red hats and wanting to take a step closer to a higher position. Although the government has now abolished the Jinhua government and established counties, Lanxi has stationed a top-ranking inspector and concurrently serving as the county magistrate of the experimental county. The political mission it bears is much greater than that of the former government officials. Moreover, "things in the world never come singly." The current magistrate of Jinhua County happens to be an outstanding subordinate of the Lanxi County government, who was promoted over the clouds. No wonder the political effectiveness of these two "sister counties" shows special progress compared to other places.

Before the center of transportation shifted elsewhere, the boats crowded in the port every night often blocked the heart of the river. Just five years ago, the transportation companies were still very developed. The water merchants sent by the major rice shops in Shanghai and Hangzhou to buy rice here usually numbered fifty to sixty people. Now, many transportation companies have closed their doors invisibly, and the water merchants who regularly reside in Lanxi are no more than a few people. The old tycoons of Guanxi were almost all in the ham and medicinal materials industries. Currently, the ham industry is affected by the ham companies in northern Jiangsu. The medicinal materials industry is even more declining due to the increasing popularity of Western medicine. The number of people buying expensive deer antlers and weighing ginseng has become scarce. Therefore, both of these businesses are suffering from chronic diseases. The rural economy is also in decline. The things that ordinary people and poor farmers send to the pawnshops are extended from the October deadline to twenty-four months, but no one goes to redeem them. The extension is not due to the pawnshops' generosity but because the clothing shops that consume the pawned clothes have not encountered customers with "ten thousand strings of cash." The main reasons for this are the "January 28th Shanghai Incident," "the opening of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Road," and the "drought of the 23rd year." Since last autumn, the slight increase in grain prices, especially the increase in tung oil prices, has indeed provided some relief to the rice and oil-producing rural areas. If the grain price can consistently maintain a price of three to four yuan per picul, then the Lanxi market, which has gradually shown signs of recovery this summer, will not be difficult to embark on a prosperous road to a moderately prosperous society.

Hu Ciwei, the magistrate of Lanxi Experimental County, was originally a cadre instructor at the Central Political Science School. The reason why he was transferred here to be the magistrate was accompanied by the task of cultivating experimental political talents. All graduates of the Central Political School, whose studies are similar to the nature of county-level administration, must first come here for practical training (about two months) before being assigned to actual work. Since the experimental county government bears this mission, it pays special attention to local political facilities and wants to make it a progressive and rational model county. This goes without saying.

Hu, as a scholar, left school to serve as the magistrate. He has done several things in a decisive manner, causing the people to feel a sense of fear. Lanxi has developed water and land transportation, with people from all directions. Many people are addicted to red pills. The annual leakage of expenditure on buying drugs is estimated to be no less than hundreds of thousands of yuan. Although the government has issued orders to ban it, the cases are handled by the court. The wealthy are fined one thousand or eight hundred yuan to supplement the court's expenses. The poor cannot be imprisoned for a long time and fed with food rations, which makes the situation even worse, with no achievements at all. In the 23rd year of the Republic, drug offenders were handed over to the county government for handling. Hu began with strict enforcement and successively executed seventeen or eight drug offenders. Among them, an eighty-three-year-old woman also lost her life due to drug trafficking. Everyone realized that the law was inexorable and had a sense of caution. Not only have the cases of drug trafficking and drug use gradually disappeared, but also the petty thieves who have associated with them have disappeared.

There is also a kind of local ruffian force here, which is also a semi-public secret organization that arbitrarily moves flowers and grafts trees, falsely setting penalty clauses, and heavily exploiting merchants. Merchants from other places have suffered from their losses. They say, "It is difficult for evil dragons to fight local snakes," and they can only swallow their anger like a mute eating coptis. Hu learned the details and silently designed to capture four or five of their leaders and send them to Hangzhou, where they are still confined. In this way, he naturally won the applause of the merchants.

The day the reporter arrived in Lanxi from Jinhua, it was raining heavily. A city gate called "Yuyue Gate" was flooded a foot deep. In a place where passers-by gathered to take shelter from the rain, I unintentionally talked to the common people about the political situation of this experimental county magistrate. In addition to complimenting him for his ability, some said that he was too strict. If the common people owed grain or money, regardless of landlords or poor farmers, someone with a gun would immediately come to chase them to the county government to live in a house without money. Therefore, in the past, only 50-60% of the grain tax was collected each year. This county magistrate has been able to collect 100% in recent years. The person who spoke these words also stuck out his tongue at the end to supplement the lack of tone. Originally, the so-called good governance in ancient times should consider both law, order and human feelings. The collection of land tax everywhere, as long as it is not arbitrary taxation, and can be taken from the people and used for the people, is of course beyond reproach. However, for the impoverished farmers who have experienced natural disasters and man-made disasters, in order to avoid the loss of killing the goose for eggs, it may not be a way to cultivate the people's morale.

Visiting Magistrate Hu at the county government, Hu came out to meet me. In addition to general conversation, he also talked about some of his feelings after becoming an official. One thing is worth noting. He said that the common people are originally very good, but the government has lost credibility and is too sorry for them. The so-called "water can carry a boat, but it can also capsize it," and the future is very dangerous. Last time, there was a severe drought in Lanxi. The county government organized a food loan cooperative to provide relief, lending without interest and repaying after the autumn harvest. But the disaster victims were like birds frightened by the bow, preferring to starve rather than easily accept food. Finally, when they were on the verge of starvation, they gradually came to borrow food. However, there were still words like "supporting the county government to earn interest." Later, when the county government actually did not charge interest, it regained its credibility. Even such food loan relief is not easy to gain the trust of the people. If a larger people's power is needed, wouldn't it be even more difficult? What Hu said is true. For example, Zhejiang once conducted a land declaration a few years ago, which cost 4 million yuan. Lanxi County alone was assigned 100,000 yuan, but the declaration yielded no results. Later, in fact, it was necessary to conduct another investigation, touching the people's sore spots, and naturally there would be resentment. For example, in recent years, the requisition of civilian land and fields to build roads and railways was said to be compensated in advance, but in reality, it was just empty talk. Therefore, this time, the counties have raised money for aviation birthday celebrations. Huang Ming, the county magistrate, is cautious and careful, which is very right. Because China is in a period of serious national crisis, on the one hand, material construction and national defense construction are, of course, very urgent, but on the other hand, cultivating the people's strength and cultivating the people's hearts are also equally fundamental plans. If the foundation of the fundamental plan has not been built firmly, then all other material suggestions will naturally not be easy to be as stable as a rock.

Lanxi has many mountains and few plains, so there is a shortage of arable land. The average arable land per capita is only two mu, so life is felt to be insufficient. The average utilization rate has reached 99%, and there is very little hope of expanding arable land. Moreover, according to general observation, tenants account for 80% of the total number of farmers, and land rights tend to be concentrated in the hands of a few people. Since the county was reformed as an experiment, after rectifying public security, it has been engaged in land investigation. The county government has paid attention to the research on improving agricultural affairs, reorganizing arable land, supporting owner-farmers, and making land use economical and increasing its productivity.

Five Months of Chinese Goods Exported to the US

The US Consulate General in Shanghai announced the statistics for Chinese exports to the US in the first five months of this year, totaling US$35,636,877, with May accounting for US$6,963,322. However, silver shipped to the US in recent months has not been included in the statistics. Among the exports in the five months, hides and manufactured goods accounted for the most, totaling US$11,211,796. Plant-based foods and beverages, including peanut oil, totaled US$2,216,786. Non-plant-based foods, such as sesame, tung oil, and sesame seeds, totaled US$13,568,087. Textiles, including wool for carpets and embroidered cloth, totaled US$5,683,691. Although the demand for firecrackers this year was not large, it was more than last year, totaling US$234,372.

Increased Tax on Salt in Shanghai, Nanhui, Chuansha, and Other Counties; Increase to Seven Yuan and Two Jiao

The Shanghai County Government has approved the letter from the Songjiang Audit Branch of the Songjiang Salt Transport Deputy Commissioner's Office, which stated that it had received instructions from the Ministry of Finance, which stated that the land in Shanghai, Nanhui, Chuansha, and other counties, as well as Baoshan's Jie Yi and Jie Jiu, was designated as reduced land because private salt supervision was rampant. The tax rate was very light, far from the tax rate for soy sauce workshops. The Ministry has twice increased the light tax on edible salt by one yuan and seven jiao, but it is still one yuan and six jiao less than the soy sauce tax. Since soy sauce and food salt are in the same place, it is inevitable that soy sauce workshops will not purchase salt tax. According to the request of the Audit Office, the tax rate for reduced land in Shanghai, Nanhui, Chuansha, and Baoshan's Jie Yi and Jie Jiu should be increased by one yuan and six jiao per dan, which is equal to the tax rate in the inland areas and can be approved. However, the miscellaneous expenses for soy sauce salt are more than one yuan more than those for reduced land, so how to balance this should be ordered separately. It is ordered that the Deputy Commissioner immediately comply and increase the tax rate for reduced land in Shanghai (including the concessions), Nanhui, Chuansha, and Baoshan's Jie Yi and Jie Jiu from five yuan and six jiao to seven yuan and two jiao from the date of the order. All salt in transit should be investigated and uniformly supplemented. Therefore, it is ordered that this should be complied with. The county government has already issued a notice to inform everyone.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Orders a Strict Search for the Murderer in the Xuan Sheng Case, Sternly Directing Subordinates to Extend the Deadline by Three Days, Promising Strict Punishment if the Case is Not Solved

A Central News Agency reporter inquired yesterday at the Public Security Bureau about the investigation and pursuit of the murderer in the case involving the murdered Japanese resident. According to the official in charge of the bureau, after the case occurred, he immediately issued strict orders to his subordinates to solve the case within three days. He also selected capable personnel from within the bureau to form a special investigation team dedicated to handling the investigation and pursuit of the murderer in this case. The detectives in various branches and offices were reassigned to focus on collecting evidence related to this case. For days, the bureau's internal and external staff have been working around the clock, sparing no effort in handling this case. Although several leads have been obtained, the results of the interrogations have not yet led to a conclusive determination. The investigation is still ongoing. Yesterday, as the deadline expired, a reward of 2,000 yuan was offered for the arrest of the murderer, in the hope of discovering other clues and solving the case as soon as possible. At the same time, subordinates were sternly ordered to extend the deadline by three days, promising strict punishment if the case is not solved. The special task force, investigation unit, and detective brigade within the bureau, all detective personnel, after receiving orders, were fully mobilized. Liang Fuchu, the chief of the North Railway Station branch, after receiving orders, immediately convened all the heads of the offices to discuss methods for solving the case, encouraging his subordinates to risk their lives to solve this case, regardless of the consequences. Currently, work within and outside the bureau is exceptionally tense, and senior cadres are especially concentrating their efforts on dealing with this case. Although the extreme heat is making them quite fatigued, everyone is still working hard and showing no signs of weariness. It is expected that the case will be solved soon to fulfill their responsibilities. Regarding the protection of Japanese residents, the bureau has withdrawn the centralized training and increased police force in areas where Japanese residents live, deploying more patrol officers and patrol units to conduct close inspections at all times. It is also closely coordinating protection efforts with the police departments of the two concessions and the Japanese police.

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau issued Public Notice No. 13 yesterday, stating: "It has been found that on the afternoon of the 10th of this month, at approximately 8:00 PM, in Lane 35, Dixiwei Road and Qimei Road, a Japanese resident named Xuan Sheng Kuangzuo was attacked and killed. The Linping Road Police Station reported this case to the bureau, and the municipal government ordered subordinates to solve the case within three days. Now, according to Dispatch Order No. 19311 from the municipal government, because the perpetrator has not yet been apprehended, the following rewards are offered:

Anyone who leads police detectives to apprehend the principal offender, and whose interrogation confirms the facts, will be rewarded with 2,000 yuan in national currency.

Anyone who provides information leading to the apprehension of the principal offender, and whose interrogation confirms the facts, will be rewarded with 1,000 yuan in national currency."

You are ordered to comply accordingly. This notice is hereby issued for the information of all citizens.

July 13, 25th year of the Republic of China, Bureau Chief Cai Jingjun.

Ministry Approves Delay in Minting of Two and a Half Cent Subsidiary Coins

The Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation received instructions from the Ministry of Finance yesterday regarding the additional minting of two-and-a-half-cent subsidiary coins, stating that it should be considered after the old subsidiary coins have been withdrawn to a considerable extent. The original instruction reads: "Replaced General Dai Xi, The Ministry is promoting the new subsidiary coins, on one hand, increasing the number of mints to meet market needs, and on the other hand, examining the situation in various regions, selectively withdrawing and destroying the old subsidiary coins, in order to gradually cultivate people's habit of using new subsidiary coins, thereby avoiding the risk of price gouging. Furthermore, after investigating that merchant groups from Wuxi, Wujin, Jiangyin, and other counties in Jiangsu have repeatedly requested the withdrawal of copper coins that have flooded the market, the Ministry then instructed the three banks to investigate the situation and handle it properly in accordance with the principle of fair value. This shows that the amount of old copper coins in circulation has not decreased, and there is no increase in the hardships of small-scale industry and commerce. The request to add two-and-a-half-cent coins should be considered in the future when the old subsidiary coins have been withdrawn to a considerable extent, and you should inform others of this order."

Federation of British Industries Plans to Send Chinese Students to Practice Engineering Materials

A.J. Percival, Chairman of the Selection Committee of the Federation of British Industries, wrote to this newspaper yesterday, stating: "To the Editor of Shen Bao, Two and a half years ago, the Federation of British Industries in London initiated a plan to send Chinese students to the United Kingdom to study engineering. The implementation of this plan has been satisfactory. Since then, twenty-nine Chinese students have benefited from it. Of the eight who have returned to their home countries after completing their studies, most have returned to their original positions, while a few have taken jobs at machinery companies. This student exchange plan is based on the recommendations of the British Far East Economic Mission of 1931, which felt that Chinese students' industrial training in other countries was primarily for the benefit of those countries. The objectives of this plan can be divided into commercial and cultural aspects. Commercially, it provides Chinese students with the opportunity to receive practical training in the United Kingdom, so that upon their return to China, they can use the British engineering knowledge they have acquired to solve China's engineering problems. Culturally, it can promote friendship between China and the United Kingdom. This plan is managed in China by a Selection Committee organized by prominent British engineers in Shanghai. The Federation of British Industries in London regularly informs the Committee of vacancies for internships in British factories. Notices of these vacancies are published in Chinese newspapers and announced at prominent Chinese universities such as the University of Hong Kong. Applications for each vacancy must undergo rigorous scrutiny, and only those who are deemed qualified are recommended to London for a final decision. The strict selection criteria are based on each student's specialized knowledge, experience, character, English proficiency, and physical appearance. Training in British factories involves a balanced rotation through various departments, in order to achieve a comprehensive result.

Scholarships are awarded for one year, and may be extended for another year if the work report is satisfactory. Upon the students' return to China, the Shanghai Selection Committee continues to liaise with them and strives to find them suitable employment, so that they can apply what they have learned. According to observations from participating factories and many nationally renowned companies, the breadth of the selection scope stipulated in this plan cannot be matched by any other approach. Each participating company provides the students with a small weekly stipend, supplemented by scholarships, to ensure that they can live comfortably. British shipping companies and Dutch and German companies also offer reduced fares. The Committee of London Chinese University and the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund in Nanjing have also provided some support, but the amount is too small to match China's needs and the capabilities of British industry. The Chinese people and government authorities eagerly expect the progress of the Chinese economy to depend heavily on the supply of trained engineers. If you can widely publicize the Federation of British Industries Scholarship Program, so that funds can be raised in the future to prepare for it, any British individuals or organizations who are passionate about the development of commerce and cultural exchange between China and the United Kingdom, whether through monetary or other assistance, would be greatly appreciated. Chairman of the Selection Committee of the Federation of British Industries (A.J. Percival)."

Chen Bingding Returns to China to Inspect Agriculture, Petitions the Ministry of Industries to Utilize Wasteland for Agricultural Reform

Chen Bingding, an honorary consultant of the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee and an overseas Chinese from Batavia, Dutch Java, has returned to China to inspect agriculture. Yesterday, he petitioned the Ministry of Industries to utilize wasteland for agricultural reform. The original petition is recorded below:

I respectfully submit that since the Ming Dynasty, the islands of Nanyang have successively become colonies of various Western countries, regarded as inexhaustible treasures. Those who reclaimed mountains and forests were mostly overseas Chinese. However, our government in the past neglected these distant lands and could not assist the East India Company as the British government did to claim its territory. Initially, they devoted themselves to cultivation, but ultimately, like birds hunted after use, it is truly regrettable.

According to historical records, merchants from Guangdong province who went to the Nanyang Islands generally used sailboats to transport large quantities of sugar, tea, dried longan, dried lychee, persimmons, vegetables, utensils, and other goods to sell to the local people. This was the vanguard of our overseas Chinese expanding abroad. Upon returning, they purchased local products such as sea cucumber, shark fin, buffalo horn, buffalo hoof, buffalo bone, bird's nest, rhinoceros horn, bear bile, ivory, black and white pepper, and other medicinal materials and miscellaneous goods to sell in China.

Taking Java as an example, the traces of our people's pioneering efforts have a history of over six hundred years. Three hundred and twelve years ago, the Dutch government, to develop Java's commerce, sent General Pieterzoon Coen to conquer Batavia. After a considerable time, he did not succeed and sought assistance from Mr. Su Mingwang, an overseas Chinese (originally from Tong'an, Fujian, who operated an oil mill in Banten). Mr. Su selected 500 elite overseas Chinese to assist, and they succeeded in conquering the local people. The Dutch East India Company appointed Mr. Su as Kapitan (captain). From then on, more and more Chinese people went to Nanyang. At that time, the Dutch territories were desolate, roads were not built, vegetation was dense, and animals roamed freely. Our overseas Chinese, for the sake of livelihood, did not fear hardship and went straight ahead, guiding the locals on how to reclaim land and how to plant crops. Thus, what was once useless land gradually became a source of wealth.

In the last hundred years or so, science has flourished, and Western production technology is useless in China. In addition, the Dutch government selected and dispatched specialists to dedicate themselves to guidance, resulting in significant achievements. For example, using machinery for manufacturing and improving the selection of varieties have greatly increased yields. Previously, Java needed to import sugar and tea from our country, but now it has become a famous sugar and tea-producing region in the world. The speed of its progress is truly astonishing. Other products, such as coconuts, rubber, black and white pepper, corn, citronella oil, coffee, tapioca starch, sago flour, kerosene, electric oil, and tin mines, also have large outputs. Various fruits not only meet the needs of the more than sixty million people in the Dutch territories but can also be transported abroad for sale. The above only mentions the most prosperous and largest industries; there are many other local products with considerable quantities, too numerous to list.

If production is abundant, then financial resources are sufficient, and all administrative affairs can be improved. Today, people from various countries who visit this place cannot help but marvel at it as a paradise. Examining the reasons for this achievement, our overseas Chinese have played a significant role. These overseas Chinese occupy an important position in the Dutch islands. Many operate large, medium, and small stores, and there are also many who engage in agricultural land, real estate, and factories for firewood, rice, coconut oil, citronella oil, tapioca starch, sago flour, and rubber. However, the majority are laborers. Previously, the locals were lazy, lacked knowledge, and lived simple lives, causing various industries to lag behind. With the hard work and dedication of our overseas Chinese, they have been able to excel.

However, since 1912, the Dutch government has vigorously established schools in various cities and villages, and the knowledge of the locals has gradually increased, competing with our overseas Chinese in the marketplace. The businesses we operate have not been as prosperous as before. In addition, the impact of the global economic depression of 1929 and the aggressive southward policy of the Japanese have increasingly shaken the inherent position of our overseas Chinese and brought them to a dangerous situation. In recent years, the prices of various local products have plummeted, and the social economy has deteriorated to the extreme. The assets of our overseas Chinese have suffered a loss of seventy to eighty percent. If this situation is not changed, our overseas Chinese will have no foothold in the Dutch territories.

It is estimated that there are about 1.3 million overseas Chinese in that territory. Those who have relatives to rely on can barely survive, while those who have nowhere to live have uncertain futures, drifting overseas in a miserable state. Recently, there have been restrictions on entry and various harsh taxes, making it difficult for newcomers to gain a foothold. If there are no relief measures, in a few decades, overseas Chinese will disappear from the Dutch territories.

I humbly remember that Sun Yat-sen and the leaders of the Party and the country have called overseas Chinese the "mother of the revolution," and that relief efforts are one of the policies. They should not bear to sit idly by and do nothing. Although there are now "Overseas Chinese Happy Villages" and subsidies for overseas Chinese school fees, these are mere drops in the bucket and do not solve the problem. Compassion is in everyone's heart, and especially for compatriots of the same country and ethnicity, there must be a special deep affection. Leaders of the Party and the country take it as their responsibility to relieve hunger and save the drowning. There is no need for overseas Chinese to appeal. However, momentary foolishness is enough to serve as a reference for making policies and should not be rejected by the wise.

I humbly believe that to solve this difficult problem, there is no other way than to promote planting, relieve rural areas, and revitalize industry. In recent years, the central and local governments have implemented policies for promoting planting, but the results have been minimal. Why is this the case? It is because the majority of the people do not understand the benefits of planting, and their minds are stubborn and superstitious about feng shui. Hence, there is a saying, "If there is a barren mountain, no one will cultivate it; if cultivation begins, there will be disputes!" As such, those who are enthusiastic about developing industries are hindered and cannot proceed as they wish.

Looking at Taiwan, which used to belong to our country, production was very low. But when it was occupied by the Japanese, its government vigorously promoted agriculture. Over the decades, local products have progressed almost overnight. The export value of bananas alone is over 12 million yuan per year. Other major products can be seen from this. Given the vastness of our country's territory, if our government can issue a clear decree to designate all wasteland in various provinces and force planting within a specified time, then in a few years, barren mountains and vast wilderness will all become areas of production.

Furthermore, our country has traditionally been an agricultural nation, but in recent years, food has been insufficient, and imports from overseas reach tens of millions annually. If such wasteland is utilized, in addition to rice and wheat, the widespread planting of millet (upland rice) and cassava will also greatly benefit the people's food supply.

Regarding the above points, our government may worry about financial constraints and be unable to proceed as scheduled. However, if it can establish a protection clause to ensure the safety of their capital, overseas Chinese will also be happy to use it. In this way, overseas Chinese will start businesses, enriching the people and the country, achieving multiple benefits in one fell swoop. The leaders of our government should not dismiss these words as trivial.

I, Chen Bingding, have personally felt that the above is complex and should be carefully examined and implemented.

Ministry of Finance's Approval: Invoices Combined with Receipts Only Need to Affix Stamps for One Type of Voucher

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously inquired with the Ministry of Finance about the stamping method for invoices with receipt properties. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance replied: The attached telegram from Jiangsu is acknowledged. The total amount listed on the delivery note is the amount receivable for the goods. If the note has "received national currency" or "received" marked on it, it indicates that the amount receivable for the goods has been received. The amount received and the amount receivable are one item, not two separate amounts. Therefore, it is not possible to combine the amount receivable and the amount received and forcibly affix stamps based on the combined amount. As for invoices that also function as receipts, since the tax rates are the same, according to Article 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, it is only necessary to affix stamps for one type of voucher. If the inspectors of Liyang County forcibly affix stamps based on the combined amount of received and receivable, it is wrong. Please request the Jiangsu Provincial Government to instruct the county government to investigate and correct this error. This is the approval.

Gang Fight Among Car Workers, Zhou Kailong's Injuries are the Most Serious

At 3:20 am yesterday, a dispute over business among cargo car workers on Taopeng Road in Yangshupu led to a gathering of dozens of people on both sides, each armed with iron rods, knives, and axes for a major brawl. As a result, three people on one side were injured: Jin You from Ningbo, Zhou Kailong from Yangzhou, and Hu Shikun from Shaoxing. All three were cut and beaten and collapsed to the ground, barely breathing. Upon receiving the report, the Yulin Road police station dispatched a large number of Chinese and Western detectives to the scene to arrest the perpetrators. Subsequently, four suspects were apprehended: Li Kui from Nanjing and Kang Youfa from Ningbo, and brought to the police station. The injured, Jin, Zhou, and Hu, were transported to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. Jin Jiayou suffered head injuries and was bandaged by the doctor. He was barely able to leave the hospital an hour later. Yesterday morning, Jin, Li, and Kang were taken to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division III. Zhang Shizhu, the lawyer from the Shanghai Municipal Council, stated that Zhou Kailong and Hu Shikun were unable to appear in court due to their injuries in the hospital. Silk Factory Workers' Restoration of Treatment Case Successfully Mediated Yesterday, Agreement Signed, Wages Increased to 45 Cents, Party and Government Jointly Issued Notice Limiting Resumption of Work This Morning

After the workers of various silk factories in Zhabei went on strike on the afternoon of the 7th to demand the restoration of their original treatment, the workers of various silk factories in Hongkou followed suit. The Shanghai Municipal Labor-Capital Mediation Committee convened a mediation committee record at 9 am yesterday and jointly issued a notice from the Social Affairs Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and the Municipal Party Headquarters, limiting the workers to resume work this morning. The details are recorded below:

Mediation Conference

The Shanghai Municipal Labor-Capital Mediation Committee convened a mediation committee at 9 am yesterday inside the Social Affairs Bureau in the city center. Those present were Chairman and Committee Member Zhu Guilin of the Social Affairs Bureau, Committee Member Jin Jiechen of the Public Security Bureau, Lu Yinchu of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Shen Huachen, Zhang Peishen, Yu Caizhang, and Xu Peixiong of the Silk Factory Trade Association, Lu Xiupu and Yang Hongmei of the Fourth District Silk Workers' Union, Yuan Yunlong and Yang Genti of the Sixth District Silk Workers' Union, and worker representatives from various factories, including Liu Sanbin and over twenty others. First, the chairman reported on the handling process. After a long period of discussion, a mediation record was signed, and the striking workers were limited to resuming work on the morning of the 15th. Qian Zhushi, the arrested worker, was released by the Public Security Bureau after investigation. The restoration of monthly registration of work and labor on Sundays and silkworm moths will be temporarily postponed. The meeting adjourned around 2 pm.

Signed Record

Shanghai Municipal Labor-Capital Mediation Committee Mediation Record Disputing Parties: Labor: Fourth and Sixth District Silk Workers' Union; Capital: Silk Factory Trade Association. The following dispute concerns wage disputes, etc. After the Committee convened mediation, the signed mediation record agreed upon by both parties is recorded as follows: (1) The wages of all female silk reeling workers in the city will be restored from 40 cents (the standard first-class wage) to 45 cents from June onwards, and the rest will be calculated accordingly. (2) Working hours: 5:00 am to 11:30 am, 12:30 pm to 5:30 pm (However, when labor literacy schools are opened, work starts at 5:00 am and ends at 6:00 pm, with one hour stipulated for reading time). (3) For employees with wages below 16 yuan, a general increase of 15% will be applied. For those with wages above 16 yuan, the factory will discretionarily increase up to 10%. Wages will be calculated monthly. This document has been agreed upon and signed by representatives of both parties, and the mediation is established and should be regarded as a collective agreement between the disputing parties.

Joint Notice

The Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau jointly issued a notice stating: This city's silk factory workers' demand for an increase in labor-capital disputes has been mediated by the Labor-Capital Mediation Committee on the 14th of this month. After both parties agreed to sign, the mediation was established. In addition to directly informing the labor-capital parties of the Labor Word No. 207 mediation record and ordering them to comply, this joint notice is issued, ordering the striking workers of each factory to abide by it and resume work uniformly on the morning of the 15th, without delay or misunderstanding. This is the notice. July 14, 25th year of the Republic of China. Standing Committee Members Tong Xingbai, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Director Cai Jingjun, Director Wu Xingya.
