An Additional Special Deposit of Three Yuan Will Be Charged for July and August Old Cotton

The China Merchants Yarn and Cloth Exchange will charge an additional cash deposit of three yuan per dan for new transactions of July and August cotton, in addition to the special security deposit already announced. (The total deposit for the July contract will be nine yuan, and the total deposit for the August contract will be six yuan.) Both sides will continue to pay the account.

Central Cotton Area Receives Showers; US Cotton Falls Back Due to Sell-Offs

Yesterday, US cotton opened with bad news from Liverpool. Foreign merchants sold, and long positions closed, leading to reactive selling. Part of Georgia and the central cotton area received showers. Each month fell by 9 to 16 points. The volume of transactions was not high. Subsequently, the market was strong in Chicago, and dealers and brokers increased buying, causing the market price to rebound. The textile market was strong and active, spot goods were firm, and sellers were scarce. Loan cotton was not sold. The closing was balanced, with spot cotton falling by 7 points and futures falling by between 7 and 14 points. English cotton spot fell by 8 points, and futures fell by 7 points. The closing and sales by Indian cotton long positions were absorbed by European exporters. Prices in Pingguo rose or fell by 1.5 to 1.75 Rupees, Aomla fell by 1 to 1.5 Rupees, and Bailuoxi fell by 1.5 to 1.75 Rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left. (Telegram dated the 13th)

Rangoon's Cotton Exports Last Week

A telegram from Bombay on the 13th stated that the amount of cotton exported from Rangoon last week was 566 tons, of which 24 tons went to Japan, 215 tons to China, and 103 tons to Liverpool.

Three-Piece Yarn Firm, Cotton Weak

A telegram from Osaka on the 14th stated that Three-Piece Yarn rose by 9 jiao to 4 yuan and 8 jiao, with the near month at 217 yuan and the far month at 209 yuan and 8 jiao. Cotton futures rose by 1.5 jiao to 4.5 jiao, with the near month at 73 yuan and 7 jiao and the far month at 66 yuan and 8 jiao and 5 jiao.

Hardware: Steel Market Stands Out

Yesterday, the hardware market saw activity as factories like Kangyuan, Nanyang, and Huacheng made purchases. 200 boxes of 90-pound tinplate opened at $18.75. 650 boxes of old steel mill goods from the Trading Company sold between $35 and $36. New steel mill goods opened at $33 to $33.25. Due to limited stock, narrow hoop iron also increased to $23. Single-coated patterned iron opened at varying prices from $26 to $28. Enamel factories disposed of 300 dan (a unit of weight) of first-cut scrap iron at $6, and 500 dan of prime-grade iron at $9.25. Battery factories and printing houses purchased 40 to 50 barrels of white lead sheets. Prices per dan were approximately $30.05 for #5, $30 for #6, $29.75 for #7, and $29.50 for thick patterned iron. The East White Iron market has been quite chaotic recently, resulting in limited offerings. The market saw little change. Due to specific demand, 7-8 boxes of #26 large tinplate opened at $75-76. Although #24 tinplate was also offered, the quantity was small, so the price remained unchanged, it is said.

Local Cotton Yarn Inventory at its Lowest; Total Inventory Counts 82,460 Bales

According to a survey by a certain foreign firm in this port, the cotton yarn inventory of Chinese, British, and Japanese factories at the end of June totaled 82,460 bales, an increase of 4,077 bales compared to the 78,383 bales at the end of May. Among them, the amount of Japanese factory yarn was 6,572 bales, an increase of 1,206 bales compared to the previous month. The amount of Chinese yarn was 75,888 bales, an increase of 2,871 bales compared to the previous month. It is found that 20-count yarn accounts for the most at 54,022 bales, an increase of 1,568 bales compared to the end of the previous month. Foodstuffs: New Wheat Abundant, Standard Market Sentiment Loosens

Yesterday's wheat market, after opening in the morning, saw slight increases in all months, but reversed and fell in the afternoon. U.S. wheat quotations: Chicago nearby down a little over 4 jiao, distant down 8 fen to 1 jiao plus; Canadian good around 2 jiao. Therefore, the initial sentiment was still calm, similar to the previous day. Later, short-covering was very smooth, and prices turned higher, up 3-4 fen compared to the previous day. December was still down 4 fen. By the time the afternoon prices opened, sentiment gradually weakened, falling nearly 1 jiao from the morning's highest price, and also down 3-4 fen compared to the previous day's closing price. Currently, market sentiment is based on the fact that the United States has received timely rain, and U.S. wheat quotations are expected to mostly decline. The domestic wheat market, with abundant arrivals, is also difficult to sustain its strength for long. Rumor has it that the flour market situation has also greatly eased, and major bulls have covertly liquidated their positions. Therefore, with these two factors working together, market sentiment has gradually loosened. Currently, the wheat market, with cargo from Zhongguan not yet opened, only opened special high-quality goods from the Jinpu Railway, such as Mingguang Guandian wheat at 4 yuan 5 jiao 5 fen, totaling 6,000 bags, handled by Fufeng. Huaian wheat at 4 yuan 5 jiao, Jiangbei wheat at 4 yuan 4 jiao 7 fen, and substandard at 4 yuan 3 fen, handled by Zhongda for 3,000 bags, it is said.

Flour Gray Market Down 4-5 Fen

Yesterday's flour market, opening both morning and afternoon, continued to follow price limits for all months. There were not many formal transactions between the two parties, but the self-dealing among brokers was quite active. The previously reported gray market situation gradually loosened because overseas wheat quotations had fallen back due to rain, and domestic demand for spot flour was also quieter. In addition, with the abundant arrival of new wheat, all factories were able to maximize production, so some bulls were no longer stubbornly holding on. Near and distant months were reportedly down to a gray market price of 3-4-5 fen. If overseas quotations continue to be unfavorable, this kind of above-the-table operation can disappear invisibly, it is said.

Rice High-Quality Goods Market Still Firm

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, various sources only arrived with a dozen or so vendors, totaling over 2,000 piculs of goods. Sales in this street had gradually become active, but suddenly suffered a closure of a certain feed store, resulting in a large batch of spot goods being released, so sales in this street became sluggish again. The wholesale of goods from both the northern and southern groups only handled about 600 bags, and although the arrival of early japonica and thin indica rice was scarce, the resulting market showed a stable to slightly soft trend. Du Yangxian was similar, with no change in the gray market price.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, over a dozen vendors arrived from various routes, and the various outlets in the market turned quiet again. Fresh white japonica prices retreated by a small number of fen to 1 jiao, while old and substandard goods were stagnant. Thin indica was high and firm, while substandard was weak. White glutinous rice prices increased. Yangpu premium rice was short by about 1 jiao. The prices of other goods were uncertain.

Silk and Tea: U.S. Price of Chinese and Japanese Silk Increases

Yesterday, the overseas silk market had a bullish sentiment. Although the sale of New York White Factory spot futures was slightly down by half a cent compared to last Saturday, the holding price of Chinese and Japanese silk actually increased by 6 fen in the U.S. The actual sales are not smooth. Yokohama silk prices remained firm as before, with spot prices unchanged and futures slightly down by 1 yuan. Shanghai silk traders are still watching and holding firm, with very few transactions. Foreign firms are only doing some intermittent trading, it is said.

Private Goods Silk Auction Not Opened Yesterday

Yesterday, the Jianghai Customs in this port solicited bids for 130-odd boxes of private goods silk. Although there were many bidders, there was a sudden dispute, so the auction was not opened. The market inventory is thin, and customers are waiting to handle the goods, so the prices in various markets have soared. Today, the price of 120-number Tianqiao brand is 415 yuan, and the price of 120-number Taiyang brand and Tiantan brand are both 400 yuan. However, the effectiveness is not significant, so households are not yet willing to sell. Only the Nanshi Silk Belt Factory purchased 20-odd boxes of Taiyang brand silk, with prices as above.

Tunxi Zhenmei Tea Sales Active in Europe

Yesterday, Tunxi Zhenmei was still quite active. Since the Jilong company greatly sold off after the price decreased the day before, Tianyu also started to handle about 400-odd boxes, with transaction prices ranging from 81 to 90 yuan. Market prices are still firm. Jardine Matheson purchased over 100-odd boxes of Tunxi oil-treated Zhenmei at a price of 114 yuan. Xiehe Tea Company purchased over 200-odd boxes of Wuyuan Northwest Township Zhenmei at prices ranging from 75 to 83 yuan. In addition, Tongfu Baolong and other firms also had scattered transactions for various teas. PingShui different color Pearl tea had been silent for many days, but turned active yesterday. Jardine Matheson purchased about 1,400-odd boxes, and Jinlong purchased about 600-odd boxes, with selling prices ranging from 56 to 58 yuan. The total sales of black and green tea in the city reached over 4,800-odd boxes. Green tea prices were stable, and black tea prices fell by 3-4 yuan. Among them, the floral fragrance category also fell by 2-3 yuan compared to the previous time.

Piece Goods: Dyed Fabric Orders Excellent, Fine Cloth Also Better Than Previous Years

Yesterday, the piece goods market gradually stabilized. Various dyeing factories are receiving orders for various colored fabrics for export in this month. Most of these orders are from the Sichuan group. Currently, they are processing and dyeing in a rush, fearing they will not be able to keep up. Spot fine cloth and fine twill are in great panic, and the spot goods in various stalls in the market have been almost completely collected. The subsequent business of adding colored fabrics is quiet for the Sichuan group, but the Shanxi and Henan groups are still adding some. Guangzhou factories and dyeing factories are selling some of the cheap fine twill and plain cloth they had previously absorbed. These are being purchased by wholesale shops, dyeing factories, and the Yangtze River group in this street, with prices slightly cheaper than the market (per piece) by 2.5 fen to 5 fen. The factories' sentiment is still firm and high, and the factories are raising the prices they are calling for, with a small amount being offered. Customer groups are buying at market prices, and sales to customers are most active along the Yangtze River, including Datong, Anqing, Nanchang, Tingzhou, and Hubei. The most popular items are this factory's fine cloth, fine twill, pigment broadcloth, straight tribute crepe, and woolen cloth, totaling over 300 pieces. The medium and lower grades of plain poplin in the market are particularly popular. The Huayang, Yufeng, Guangzhong, and other factories have sold out of exports. The stock of Tianyi goods increased by 1 fen per yard in the market. The Xiamen plain poplin factory had 60-70 boxes in stock, which were all purchased by wholesale shops in this street. The stock of striped poplin is also gradually decreasing. This year's poplin market is much better than in previous years, it is said.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Tong'an Dried Longan Harvest Hopeless; Lychee Arrives in Abundance, Selling Prices Also Loosen

The flower seedlings for Tong'an dried longan were very good this year, and a full harvest was expected. However, due to the drought recently, the newly formed fruits are falling off from time to time, resulting in a greatly reduced harvest. According to recent Tong'an communications, based on the current situation, it is predicted to be only 60-70% of what was expected. However, there may still be changes in the future.

The first batch of orchid bamboo branches, bird leaf branches, early red branches, etc., produced in Zhangzhou, only arrived in small quantities last week. Coincidentally, they ran into a sharp drop in Guangzhou branches, resulting in a large reduction in exchange prices. The higher prices were 22 yuan per package, and the lower prices were around 15 yuan. The second and third batches of orchid bamboo branches have also been transported, totaling 188 boxes from Taiyuan and Shandong. As the customs clearance procedures have not been completed, they are expected to open tomorrow. Several hundred boxes of Haikou branches and Shuidong branches opened yesterday, with prices loosening by 1 yuan to several jiao, and the lowest prices were not more than 9 yuan. Jinshan branches, Yushan branches, etc., are also continuing to fall. The production price of new glutinous rice branches is 100 yuan, and the price of dried rice branches is around 80 yuan. They have not yet arrived in Shanghai. Fresh goods of good quality are only selling for 16-17 yuan, it is said.

Snippets

— (Fang Shujun)

Living in the 20th century, the competition for survival is becoming increasingly fierce, the strong bully the weak, and the many bully the few. Weak nations are like fish in a pot, dogs without homes, oppressed by the strong everywhere. Therefore, what we need at this time is to use our clean minds and even more unsavory hands to develop our abilities and enrich our skills. If we harbor the mentality of "I only eat this bowl of rice, only wear this piece of clothing," and feel content with what we have, then we will forever be at the mercy of others. Living in the world in this way is merely occupying a space; living out one's remaining body in mediocrity is no different from being a beast. Therefore, "all the possibilities of life are like a weighing scale; it can fall to the good side, or it can fall to the bad side." Don't wait until it's all bad before you realize it, because by then, life will already be gone.

No labor or hardship in the universe is enough to be considered suffering; the greatest suffering is losing the ability to control one's own spiritual will.

Only "courage" can lead to victory, only "struggle" can lead to light, only "hard work" can fulfill our mission.

Indian Beauty

— Lan Shan

Next door to my aunt's house, upstairs in the living room, a family moved in last month—Mr. and Mrs. Ma, and their beautiful young daughter. Not long after, I don't know who racked their brains and gave her an honorary title, calling her "Indian Beauty"!

This title is a bit incongruous, but it's also quite fitting. —Even Miss Ma herself silently acknowledges it with a smile. —It's because she has a face and body of glowing dark skin. When she talks to you or yawns, her teeth, as white as seashells, compete with the shiny blackness of her face, reflecting each other and making people feel the beauty of snow in charcoal. This is further enhanced by a straight and upright jade nose, a pair of lively, round, and large black eyes, a slender and shapely figure, and liberated breasts that are still tremulous. In this light, she is almost no different from the wives of Indians. The aesthetic ideals of 1936 have already moved from the shallow praise of whiteness to the praise of black charm. What about "Black Peony," "Black Temptation," and endless cries, aren't they clear proof? All colors are false, only black is the true, powerful, and moving king of colors!

Indian Beauty also understands this principle deeply, and she is very pleased to have this kind of skin color. She is very close to my cousin—Xian—and last time she advised her: "If you want to get skin like mine, it's best to go to the Hongkou swimming pool often. After a few months, I guarantee you can succeed. —I myself can't play around anymore, for fear that the sun will shine on my face. If the skin fades, then one piece will be light, and one piece will be dark, and there's no way to fix it." But she has done her research. Xian was so moved by what she said that she asked me for advice the day before yesterday, and even wanted me to accompany her to swim every Saturday and Sunday. I said: "If you intend to become an Indian Beauty number two, you might as well: but unfortunately, you don't have a straight nose, and your eyes aren't round and big enough, it's not like it." When I said this, she also realized it.

Indian Beauty likes to wear rose-red and jujube-red clothes, which can increase her charm. I once joked with her, "Miss Ma, if you wore Indian women's clothing and ran on the road, I guarantee those Indians would start trying to become relatives with you!"

She smiled sweetly and scolded me for gossiping like everyone else! —And made me appreciate the beauty of snow in charcoal for a while.

Crispy Plum Peddler

— Zhu Shaofei

In summer, people are a bit lazy, especially in the afternoon. Sitting in the house, you feel a bit sleepy. It is said that eating sour things can wake you up, and only plums are the most delicious sour things. In the countryside, during the busy silkworm season, when "picking naps" or when the silkworms go up the mountain to "pick cocoons," if you get tired late at night, you pick a few from the plum tree, mix them with some salt, and eating them will wake you up. So in my hometown (Dongshan), plums are regarded as the only wonderful product for relieving sleepiness.

When the season enters summer, you can hear the cries of crispy plum peddlers in the villages from time to time. The crispy plum peddler's load has a round wooden bucket on one end and a square wooden tray with grids on the other. There are seven or eight kinds of plums of different sizes in the grids. The waxy yellow plums you choose are lined with a green mulberry leaf. Chewing two halves in one bite is indeed very crispy.

"Crispy plums, oh..." A series of loud and long calls pass from the entrance of the alley, gradually reaching the front of my house. The load stops under the shade of the big elm tree. Then comes the sound of "da, da," the sound of tapping the ash from the tip of the dry tobacco pipe. We children listen and come out happily to stand beside the load. The plum peddler is an old man with a white mustache and a thin braid with countable hairs. He is very amiable. Sometimes he touches our heads, or picks a few small crispy plums from the tray and shares them with us children, asking us to call him Old Grandpa. If we really call him Old Grandpa, he will open his mouth and smile happily. Even if there are no customers, he will stop for a long time before picking up the load and leaving. These scenes of the children with the old crispy plum peddler are now vividly in my mind.

It is again the season of hearing the cries of crispy plum peddlers. The same series of calls reach the alley. That old man has been dead for many years. Now the one carrying the load and calling out is his son.

The Three Movements of Dealing with the World

Resolve—deeply understand the essence

Round—social experience

Square—academic achievement

Monk Yuanming

— Zhou Xian

Monk Yuanming was one of the monks in a certain temple in my hometown. He was originally a normal school student from a neighboring county. He could talk, write poetry, and even write good Northern Wei-style calligraphy. Fifteen years ago, for some unknown reason, he abandoned his family and converted to Buddhism, asking the old abbot of the temple to tonsure him. The old abbot asked about his background and dared not take him in. After a few days, his family also tracked him down. His old mother and young wife forced him to go back, but he simply ignored them. The old abbot had no choice but to take him in, giving him the name Yuanming. Because he had a good foundation in learning, he had penetrated Zen principles in less than three years. His poems were also full of the Zen flavor of understanding the mind and seeing the nature. The local gentry had works of correspondence with him. At that time, he was only about twenty-five years old.

Another two years passed quickly. His mother and wife passed away one after another. After he returned home to take care of the funeral, he allocated half of his family property to the temple and half to the poor members of his clan. In that year, there was a war in the area, and large and small households were fleeing to avoid the disaster. Yuanming and his disciples remained peacefully in place. Three months later, the chaos subsided, but when those who had fled returned, they had lost track of Yuanming. When they asked the old abbot, they learned that a certain division commander and Yuanming were former classmates, so he took him away. A year later, Yuanming returned to the temple and bowed to the old abbot once. At that time, he was wearing a military uniform and had four guards with him, saying that he had been promoted to secretary by a certain division commander. After that, there was no news of him, and no one knew Yuanming's whereabouts.

Yesterday evening, a wandering ascetic monk suddenly came to my door, wearing ragged robes and straw sandals, with a gaunt appearance, holding a yellow book, saying that he was raising money for a certain temple in western Zhejiang to rebuild Buddhist statues. He bowed and asked me to donate. I took a closer look and seemed to recognize him. After questioning him further, I learned that he was Yuanming, whom I hadn't seen for ten years. According to him, he had been in the army for two years, and took the opportunity to escape. He wandered to Zhejiang, met a high-ranking monk, studied for several years, and became even more enlightened. This time, he was ordered by his master to go down the mountain to raise money to rebuild Buddhist statues. Once he had raised 3,000 gold coins, he would have completed his merits. He would then wander to Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu to visit famous mountains and ancient temples, in order to end the worldly ties and no longer seek a living in the human world, but to seek refuge in the place shown by his master.

After talking for a while, I only helped with two yuan because I was short of money. He bowed and thanked me and left. Before leaving, he said, "Three years later, you may be going to Shanghai. If there is a connection, there may be another chance to meet." Afterwards, some people said he was a scammer, and that there were many slippery monks and Taoists in Shanghai. But I feel that this Monk Yuanming, although not an enlightened high-ranking monk, is definitely not someone who just recites scriptures. So I wrote this down.

A Change of Mates

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 4: Sight and Sound Are Not Floating Doubts but the Exchange of Letters; Life and Death Can Be Entrusted to the Generosity of Sorrowful Sighs

Just then, two people on the side of the street laughed heartily. Guoshi's heart skipped a beat, wondering if people were laughing at him. This street was full of acquaintances, and it would be embarrassing to be laughed at. So he straightened his face, calmed his pace, and walked step by step. When he reached the place where he and the person were supposed to meet, his heart started to beat again. Today, when he sees him, will he have a happy face? An angry face? Or will he be like usual, without any color on his face? Of course, if he's happy, that means he's sympathetic. If he's angry? Then all hope will become an illusion. If he's like usual, maybe he didn't receive the letter. He immediately added a kind of indescribable pain in his heart. His hands were behind his back, and he walked to the school with his head down. In this senior elementary school, Guoshi was a most dutiful teacher, arriving at school on time, teaching class on time, and explaining in detail to the students during class. For some reason, on this day, while sitting in the lounge waiting for class, he kept scribbling on a practice book with a pencil. His left elbow supported the edge of the table, but he used his hand to support his head. Although he had a pencil in his hand and was scribbling on the practice book, he didn't know what he was scribbling. A school servant, looking inside through the glass window, asked: Mr. Zhang, don't you have class this morning? Guoshi was called and suddenly woke up, asking: Has the class bell already rung? The school servant said: It's been ringing for ten minutes. Moreover, the bell was shaken past under the window, didn't Mr. Zhang hear it? Guoshi looked out the window, and there wasn't a single student outside the classroom. He couldn't help but laugh, picked up a book on the table, and hurriedly went to the classroom. This class was originally Chinese, and Guoshi stood on the podium and flipped through the book, trying to remember which lesson he was supposed to teach. But after flipping through seven or eight pages, he still couldn't find the place to teach. The students in the seats saw the teacher searching randomly, understood something, and called out: This class is on lesson fifteen, titled Patriotic Children. (48)

Chatter

Occasional Writings on the Lake (Part 2)

— By Tianxu, a resident of West Lake

Yangshuisuan (Salicylic acid) can relieve pain and reduce fever, detoxify blood, and is mainly used to treat diphtheria. Willows during the Qingming season should be harvested for their tender shoots. Those not having experienced prolonged rain contain more effective ingredients, so it is reasonable to harvest them in season. Mugwort and calamus must be harvested during the Dragon Boat Festival because after that, continuous plum rains will diminish their effectiveness. Ancient prescriptions often specify harvest times, mostly based on the knowledge gained from investigating the nature of things. As for the Dragon Boat Festival gifts, geese and zongzi (glutinous rice dumplings) are often presented. Geese are those born in the same year, just reaching maturity at this time, to be offered to teachers. It is the filial piety of younger generations. Geese also have other uses, such as guarding the gate, watching for guests, and removing weeds and duckweed. Their droppings serve as fish feed. Their eyes, when viewing people, act like convex lenses, which is the opposite of cow eyes. The pupils of cows act as magnifying glasses, so they see children as adults, hence they are controlled by them. The pupils of geese act as reducing glasses, so even when they see adults, they perceive them as small, thus they dare to peck at them and make loud, harsh noises. During the Dragon Boat Festival, hiring a cat involves offering salted food. Cats with a light palate are more likely to hunt mice, while those who prefer salty food will steal food. This is similar to choosing a son-in-law, where one seeks a male known for his ability to scare away mice. Only those seeking an heir would seek a female. Zongzi are made with aged glutinous rice. After the plum rains, the rice will be infested with weevils, so it is steamed and stored during this time, to be used as lunch in the fields. The poet's line, "Steam ginseng and cook glutinous rice towards the eastern fields," reflects the reality of men plowing and women weaving. Summer rice paddies are prone to diseases, often with damp heat accumulating internally, leading to malaria in the autumn. Therefore, glutinous rice, which can induce sweating, is eaten with goose, also as an agent to draw out the disease, and to prevent the onset of typhoid fever and dysentery in the autumn. This is similar to the principle of vaccinating against smallpox between spring and summer to prevent its spread. In the past, during the Dragon Boat Festival, street vendors would sell festive items, calling them "mugwort tigers, peach and willow charms," for women to wear in their hair to prevent dragonflies and other insects from flying onto their heads and causing earaches. As for sachets and armbands, they always contained camphor to prevent lice between the collar and sleeves. If rhubarb was worn as an amulet, it prevented the transmission of typhoid fever. Taking Chen Wuji's San Yin Fang as if there was no time to lose, using sweating and vomiting was not enough, they used purging, enabling it to cure with a single purge. This truly is what is called "a lotus that prolongs life," each fitting the charm of the season. Therefore, I have always thought that seasonal customs lead every household and every person to follow without being taught, all willing to do things that benefit themselves and others. They become accustomed to it naturally and unconsciously, and they are not bothered by the trouble or the expense. This is what we call "decree," truly encompassing the fullness of command. It is unknown who first initiated it, but they could make the people believe and follow so readily. In today's world, everyone has the right to freedom. One can neither command nor decree. Any kind of movement, wanting it to be universally popular and spontaneously followed, is indeed extremely difficult. Therefore, I believe that in reforming and improving, what is not good should be changed. But good customs and habits should not be regarded as superstitions to be completely overthrown. We should rather pay close attention to protecting them, lest they be lost. The so-called seasonal rituals are also the rituals of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame. "Entering a country, inquire about its customs" means that the customs practiced must have deep meanings. The son enters the ancestral temple every year to perform rituals precisely because he fears not knowing the proper etiquette. If etiquette is lost, seek it in the countryside. I happened to be in a rural village during the Dragon Boat Festival and felt that the lingering mist and smoke were like the haze used for air raid defense. If air raid defense could be conducted in this way, what difficulty would there be in driving away iron birds? We could mobilize the masses to capture and eliminate them, just like catching snakes and tigers, which is not impossible. "The people can be made to follow it, but cannot be made to understand it." I have always believed that the phrase should be punctuated after "can," but sometimes it is better to read it as a whole phrase for ingenious application. For example, building towers was originally for reconnaissance, to defend against enemies and provide observation. Fearing public panic, they used divine teachings to prevent immorality and delusion. Today's highways are also intended for the convenience of transportation and sightseeing, perhaps similar to the strategy of "openly repairing the plank road while secretly crossing Chencang." But if there is no defense, it can be used by the enemy. How to defend? Our ancestors had methods of mutual assistance and surveillance. Isn't today's Baojia system similar? "Ten years of instruction, aiming to destroy Wu," but at the time, they certainly did not explicitly state it to avoid provoking Wu's suspicion. "Preventing the people's mouths is more difficult than preventing rivers." Is this what is meant by "the people can be made to follow it, but cannot be made to understand it?"

The Southwest Shows Hope for Resolution

— He

According to yesterday's telegram from Beijing, the Military Affairs Commission issued a personnel order on the 13th, appointing Yu Hanmou as the Director of Pacification of Guangdong, Commander-in-Chief of the Army, and concurrently Commander of the 1st Army of the 4th Army. Yu has already left Beijing on the same day to return to his defense area. There is hope for a resolution of the situation in Guangdong. However, according to a telegram from Hong Kong, Huang Xuchu suggested that Guangdong and Guangxi strengthen economic cooperation, and Guangdong agreed to allocate 20 million to help Guangxi. Huang immediately returned to Nanning by plane. The saying that Miao Peinan was executed by shooting, if viewed in light of the second message, means that the situation in Guangdong and Guangxi is still difficult to be optimistic about.

The saying goes, "The three treasures of a country are land, people, and politics." Therefore, these three are the lifeblood of establishing a country, and not private rights to be protected. The authorities in Guangdong and Guangxi have disobeyed the orders of the central government, forming a situation of separatism, which has lasted for several years, so that the domestic politics cannot be fully on track, and it is seen as a disorderly country. This responsibility is difficult for the Southwest authorities to evade, because a country with more than two governments, each governing separately and not under the same jurisdiction, this kind of畸形 organization is rarely seen in other countries. If there is no unity internally, how can there be anything to say externally?

"Settle the internal affairs before resisting external aggression" is originally a fixed step. If the internal affairs are not settled, the strength is scattered, and there is naturally no ability to resist external aggression. Now that the situation in North China is precarious, the authorities in Guangdong and Guangxi are still using the beautiful name of resisting the enemy and carrying out the strategy of disrupting the rear, which is helping the enemy to attack themselves. If this situation is not first solved, there will be no results externally, and it will lead to destruction internally. Therefore, Mr. Yu Hanmou said that spiritual unity and unified national salvation are the fundamental plans. If there is no unity, how can there be unification? If there is no unification, how can there be national salvation? The trend of the situation cannot be denied.

Our country is a scientifically backward country, and most of our military supplies depend on various countries. If the forces are not divided and united to resist the disaster, we are still worried that it will be difficult to control the chances of victory. If we are divided into two, the effectiveness of resisting foreign aggression will be even smaller. If the Southwest cannot take care of the overall situation and ends up resisting the central government, then if a civil war breaks out, the country will be destroyed immediately. Every point of strength lost in the civil war is a point of strength reduced against foreign aggression. If this valuable strength is wasted in the civil war, how can it not be a pity?

Therefore, no matter how the Southwest authorities propagandize, no matter how strongly they argue, if they violate the eight characters of spiritual unity and unified national salvation, they are traitors to the country and abandoned by the people. Starving Man

— Lin Na

In the middle of July, I took leave from Zhoufu and came to Manila. As I came out of the train station, I immediately thought of De. He was my colleague from the time I was in Lao Fu Man, a quiet young man. I walked, stepping into the not-so-familiar courtyard, full of mud and dampness, surrounded by a collapsed fence, and only after climbing a dirty, corroded staircase did I reach that small, airless room. He had lived here for more than four months, and during these four months, he had been living in a state of semi-starvation.

The door was ajar, I knocked lightly twice, and then pushed it open. The room was so dark, without sunlight, and not a breath of fresh air could be felt. The stench of alcohol and the smell of corroded mildew filled the air. I stood outside the door for a while, feeling only faintness and silence. But soon I saw in that tiny corner a cot, on which lay a gaunt, half-naked human body.

He was breathing so peacefully and evenly, his mouth gaped wide to one side, his whole body curled up like a caterpillar. How sweetly he slept! Thinking this, I walked in and sat down on an orange crate.

The room was very cramped, filled with bottles, dirty shirts, and a few books with torn covers, lying scattered haphazardly on the floor, on the table, and on the wooden shelves. I carefully scrutinized every object and thing. After about five minutes, suddenly the half-naked body stirred slightly, and then I heard a low, weak sigh. He was awake. His tired, burning eyes stared at me in surprise, and after a moment, he murmured faintly: "It's you! My friend, you've come at just the right time!" Then he turned his eyes away from me, to the other side, and thoughtfully climbed out of bed, softly humming a popular, vulgar song.

I didn't say a word. How surprised I was by his abnormal behavior! Was this how a warm-hearted friend would treat me with such coldness? I lowered my head in anguish.

He silently and unhurriedly picked up his clothes from the bed and the rack and put them on. The turbid, stifling alcoholic fumes, like his whistling, swirled around the room, clearly showing that his drunkenness had not completely worn off. He put on his dirty shirt, pulled on his grease-stained work pants, and then snatched an old straw hat from the rack, put it on, and told me in a low voice: "Now, it's time for us to go, my friend. I believe you've just returned from Zhoufu. You mustn't be feeling tired, right?" I shook my head, and then he let out a hysterical laugh and ran down the stairs.

Passing through the accumulated mud and the collapsed old fence, a turn led to the street. The July sun was blazing, it was already about ten o'clock, the street was very quiet, and a few carriages, driven by panting, skinny horses, were lazily running along. We silently chose the shady places to walk, he had become so melancholy and depressed, alcohol had completely ruined him. After about fifteen minutes, he suddenly stopped at the entrance of a basement pub, his eyes shining with suspicious light, glancing at me. His thin lips, tinged with purple-black, trembled slightly. Without much delay, the filthy door swallowed him up. After a moment of contemplation, I followed him in.

The waiter expertly filled his glass, and he, without saying a word, fixed his burning eyes on the glass and took a large gulp. Then, his cheeks turned from pale to flushed, and his eyes shot out blazing flames.

"My friend," he exclaimed excitedly, a cunning smile on his face, "I think you must be very surprised." I softly spoke my thoughts, and he laughed loudly. "You are now a gentleman, and I, what am I? An unemployed man, a starving man waiting for the end to come. From friends, you may have heard what a bad life I've been living. Because I love my country, I constantly exposed in society their schemes to buy enemy goods in large quantities and deceive their own compatriots by changing the labels to domestic products, so they dismissed me, completely driving me into a state of starvation. However, I believe in myself, there is nothing wrong with loving my country! You see, I drink heavily; that doesn't matter, my friend, you must know that I am creating a career for my own beliefs."

His words were so casual and disorganized that I felt he was just talking drunkenly, so I knitted my brows in doubt. But he called out seriously:

"You don't believe me?" Then he shook his head despairingly and said: "You are already a gentleman, we are not on the same path, so you will never understand me. But, you watch, in the near future..." He angrily stood up from his seat, waved lightly towards the counter, and walked out. I was stunned, the sting in my heart made me lower my head.

A week later, I hurriedly returned to Zhoufu from Manila. On the way, I ran into an acquaintance, who told me that he had been arrested two days ago; because he had led many unemployed ruffians, carrying knives and bombs, to blow up those Overseas Chinese shops that sold enemy goods. I bowed my head with emotion, and murmured to myself: "De, you did the right thing!..." I felt a slight moisture in my eyes.

The Courtyard

— Hu Wei

I have returned to my hometown. When the small steamer stopped at the pier, the noisy cries of vendors and the arguments of rickshaw pullers touting for customers, that kind of familiar local accent, evoked infinite sadness in me. It has been five years since I returned to my hometown!

The family was very happy. They were busy cleaning up my room for me. Because my younger brother got married the year before last, three new buildings were built behind the house. My mother wanted me to live in the new house so that the brothers, who had not seen each other for many years, could be close. If I also got married soon, there would still be empty space on both sides of the new house, and the two buildings could be expanded to five or seven. But I love the courtyard in the old house. My former bedroom faced that courtyard, and I spent a lot of time and energy turning that courtyard into a small garden. Of course, in the past five years, the courtyard has collapsed beyond recognition. I told my mother that I was afraid that I would stay longer this time, and I wanted to restore the courtyard to its old appearance before moving to the new house to live with my younger brother.

It was already dusk, and the servants were busy cleaning my old bedroom. Closed for five years, the house had a pungent, musty smell. But the tables and chairs were very familiar to me, and were all my favorite objects. These things had been separated from me for five years, and now I felt as happy as if I had returned to the arms of an old lover. I took off my long gown and helped the servants sweep, putting the homecoming books on the bookshelf, and hanging up the pictures I liked on the walls. I put some books that I liked to read on the desk. Before dinner, the bedroom had returned to its appearance five years ago.

At dinner, my younger brother bought a bottle of wine, and everyone drank happily. My mother covered her face with the wine cup and began to nag about me getting married. Because it was rare for the whole family to gather together happily, I couldn't bear to hurt the old woman's heart. I agreed. In the evening, we talked in my room until very late.

As soon as I arrived in the countryside, my life changed immediately, and because I was thinking about the courtyard, I got up as soon as the rooster crowed behind the house. I first pushed open the window and jumped into the courtyard. In the courtyard, in addition to the osmanthus tree and the pomegranate tree, whose branches and leaves were growing more luxuriantly, the flowers and plants I planted had all become empty pots lined up on the stone slabs, and the empty space was covered with long weeds. I couldn't even see the location of the goldfish tank in front of the window. I jumped back in, took out the sickle hidden under the closet, and with a small stool, went to the courtyard to cut the grass. When the sun had risen halfway into the sky, my mother called at the door from outside. "How soundly you sleep!" she shouted as she knocked on the door.

I opened the door, covered in sweat and holding mud in my hands, which made my mother laugh.

"You're still like a child, wanting to do everything you think of. You've just come back, you should rest for a few days. Cutting grass, you can ask Afu to do it, why do you have to make such a mess?"

In fact, I knew that as long as I came home, my mother would be happy with anything. She immediately told the maid to pour water and bring out breakfast.

In the afternoon, I went to visit a few relatives, which was the custom in the countryside. When I was studying, I had to visit each family during the winter and summer vacations.

The sun set and I returned home. My younger brother was a teacher at the village primary school, and he had to be on duty one day a week. My sister-in-law told me that he was staying at the school today. My mother had also gone out in the afternoon and had not returned. This house seemed to have changed its appearance. Since my father passed away, my mother had wanted me to get married. She said:

"The family is so desolate, only if both of you get married, will it be lively again..."

Now my younger brother is married, isn't he? But I only feel more lonely. I went back to my room, looked at the dilapidated courtyard, and roused myself to remove the weeds, only the courtyard was not unfamiliar to me!

My mother came back, calling my name in the main room, and the voice gradually came closer to my bedroom:

"Xiong'er, I've begged for many flower seeds, and I also asked your uncle for two pots of lotus flowers..." She hurriedly stepped into the room, and I was dragging a pair of shoes and standing in front of the window when she said again: "You child, really..."

She handed me the flower seeds, there were climbing morning glories, stone wax red, impatiens, and a few without pistils, I couldn't name them. I took the flower seeds, and felt uncomfortable again. My mother had probably gone to each family to beg for flower seeds for me for most of the day. Naturally, after my father passed away, my mother's energy was focused on the two of us brothers, but her "energy" was only hoping that we would marry wives soon so that she could hold her grandchildren as soon as possible. I couldn't accept her "energy," and for five years I had been drifting in the city, although she had written many letters, as long as I was at home, she would never tie me down to marriage. The year my younger brother got married, she urged me to come home again, but I always ignored her, year after year, until now, when I had to come home for my father's burial next month.

My mother knew that I liked the courtyard, knew that I liked planting flowers, and she immediately took the trouble to beg for so many flower seeds. But on the other hand, I knew her consistent "energy," she wanted to keep me at home and marry a wife as soon as possible to make her happy.

Sure enough, she talked to me about that matter. My mother almost shed tears, she said:

"Your younger brother has married, and if you don't marry, the relatives will say that I am biased. Originally, the custom in the countryside is to marry in order, but that is already breaking the rules."

As a son who had not returned home for five years, I could no longer hurt the old woman's heart.

The courtyard was gradually restored to its former appearance: the flower pots on the stone steps reflected each other in red and green, the morning glories climbed high up the wall, the leaves of the two pots of lotus flowers emerged from the water, and the goldfish were swimming in the tank. I was living in the old environment again.

My mother wanted me to move to the new house to live with my younger brother again. I understood what she meant, the new generation should live in new houses, which could foretell the prosperity of the family.

From morning to night, my younger brother was a husband with a wife, and he seemed very fascinated by his current stable life. I felt that the young people of our time were so far apart. In this family, I was a loner. Every day, I still lived a lonely life in the old bedroom (now renamed the study) facing the courtyard.

The courtyard was restored to its appearance five years ago under my efforts, but what about the me and my family five years ago? I often asked myself this.

Whether to be a bird soaring in the sky, or to be my mother's filial son, I lived in contradiction...

Storytelling

Qian Jingzhang Qian Zuixian Mao Jiashu

Chinese-Western (1040) 10:00 AM to 10:45 AM

Opening "Woman Crying for Agarwood"

Autumn scenery, osmanthus fragrance in August. A passionate woman cries in her boudoir. Only hearing the sounds of cold insects outside the window are incessant. The wind blows the purple bamboo, rustling. The iron horses in front of the pole jingle. I lower my head secretly. I ponder. Thinking of the handsome young man from my maiden family. I married into the husband's family for less than half a month. The maid sent a message to my room. Saying that the young man had a disease in his teeth. I made a futile bow before the incense table. Praying to the heavens and the city god. I only wished him peace and happiness. I married into the husband's family for less than a month. The maid sent a message to my room. Saying that the young man had given up his life. I cried myself almost to death several times before I came back to life. The husband asked me why I was so sad. I only said that the pain in my abdomen was the hardest to bear. I should have come to mourn before the spirit. But I am only a bride who has not reached her full month. It is not convenient to mourn in the mourning hall. I have to secretly wear three points of mourning for you. And tie a piece of hemp cloth around my chest. A pair of embroidered shoes on hemp cloth. I asked the maid to buy a piece of agarwood. I carved the young man's handsome face. Carving him with a square scarf on his head, fluttering ribbon. White jade and black satin inlaid in the center. It's hard for me to carve you. Walking back and forth in the study. It's hard for me to carve you. Opening your mouth and calling me little sister. It's hard for me to carve you. Playing chess face to face, watching the West Chamber. It's hard for me to carve you. Urging me several times but it was hard to tell clearly. Only because the bridal sedan chair arrived at the hall. I had to harden my heart and say goodbye to the young man. When I got in the sedan chair, I cried sadly. Bystanders only talked idly. Only saying that I can't bear to leave my father and mother. Who knows. I can't bear to leave the affectionate and righteous handsome young man. Young man. I offer you on the dressing table during the day. In the evening. The green gauze curtain is made into a shrine. There are so many sad things in the world. Other people's sadness can be grieved. My sadness is hidden in my abdomen.

Zhou Zhenyu's Righteous Demon Biography

Yuan Chang (1120) 12:45 AM to 1:30 AM

Opening "Surprise and Blessing" (Mimi Collection Inaugural Issue)

Waiting for the Moon in the West Chamber, the moon is gradually deep. Hongniang accompanies the beautiful young lady. Wanting to stay at the Inn of No Return. Two golden hairpins separate the cloud-like temples. The double pearl earrings flutter. The white silk shirt is blown by the wind, emitting a strange fragrance. Jade bracelets face golden bracelets. Beads hanging on the chest gleam. Silk cloud trousers with embroidered flowers. Pink skirt flashing, slender waist and graceful figure. Embroidered shoes winding through the flower street. Seeing the peonies wither at the Peony Pavilion. Walking to the front of the Night Cloud Pavilion, I looked up. Seeing nine lotus lanterns hanging in front of the pavilion. Wishing to meet Zhang Junrui. Meeting a confidant under the Hall of Eternal Life. He has worked hard and worried a lot. And he is like Kongming in the Three Kingdoms. The bright moon shines in the Emerald Garden. In Jinbu Garden, he runs and analyzes things like a god. I only hope to complete the wedding soon. I only hope to call my son early and make a name for myself. I only hope that the official will pick osmanthus in the autumn. A hundred-year couple will form a Zhu Chen alliance. Forever reunited, not old.
